supplement my income and keep my COBOL skills up-to-date.  I am looking for
something I can work on during my off hours and on weekends.

I have a PC with all the software (I think) to make me self-supporting. I
also have been programming in COBOL (MVS) for just over 8 years.  I also
know (and teach) MVS Assembler (but would rather not take on any Assembler
work from home).

Bill Fink

Bill,

    My opinion is that it sounds like you're up to your neck with
commitments. Yes, it is very easy to get in over your head. I'm sure you

    As far as getting people to know you're available, other than word of

careful with these people.

    If you're going to do this the right way, I would suggest setting
yourself up as an S-CORP for IRS purposes. The cost is about $300-$500
through a lawyer. Make sure that when you take on a project, you sign a
contract with the company and agree upon the time-period for payment, which
is usually in the contract. You may want to seek the advice of a CPA as
well. Past experiences specifying 'DBA' with an SSN could possibly raise a
red-flag with IRS and could cause you some grief. However, if you go the
Techno-Pimp route, you may be able to work something out with them.

    Please note that I am a full-time independent consultant. Your mileage
may vary....

"William R. Fink" <bfink@spam.apci.net> wrote:

>I know this is off the subject of COBOL (sort of).
>
>I have been considering "Moonlighting" by working on COBOL programs during
>my "OFF" hours.   Are there any of you who do this kind of thing?
>

Well, I've been telecommuting from my home for the past 3yrs.  I've
also got someone "moonlighting" for me, and he does work from his
home, as does another contractor who works for me full time.  But
since I have to work with 2 other guys, who work different hours, it
can turn into 10-12hr work days.
http://www.teo-computer.com/dev/telecom.html

>During the day, I am a web application programmer (no COBOL there) and would
>like to keep my skills up in COBOL.  Primarily because I teach COBOL at the
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>

Telecommuting part-time as a moonlighter is very very difficult to get
hired for.  My moonlighter guy, has specific application skills that
got him the work.  

Perhaps Y2k work might be a possibility.

But, I'd also look at COBOL/CGI and/or NetExpress considering your
backround.

>
>How do you drum up business (other than word of mouth)?

I've gotten my work through experience and reputation.  However, I
also send out pocket calendars with my business name address info, and
they have gotten me business.  It cost me $300, but netted me $10,000.

>
>Did you need the assistance of a lawyer?

No, but a good bookkeeper or accountant helps alot.  When I got
started, I kept my previous sub-contract agreements, got blacked out
copies of contracts from other contractors, and Quicken Lawyer
(originally I used It's Legal).  I make my own contracts.  And with
high grade paper and company logo, you'd think a lawyer drew it up.

BTW, I decided to go this route and bypass the use of a lawyer because
of the no more than 20 minutes of work a lawyer spent on me when I
incorporated 10yrs ago for $500.  All she did was fill out a
"fill-in-the-blank" incorporation form, put it in a fancy binder, and
call the state and register the corporation name.  Quicken Lawyer will
do much of the same for contracts.

However, if I was in business with others, I'd use a lawyer.

If you do use a lawyer, accountant and/or bookkeeper, don't use the
yellowpages to find one.  Get one, based on referrals.

>
>What TAX considerations did you need to make?

For moonlighting, 1099 (or more accurately, sole proprietor) work is
probably the easiest to get started.  But, I'd never hire you as a
sole proprietor to do work for a client of mine, because of Section
1706.  I'd hire you as W2, unless you would incorporate.  If you work
direct to a company/client (ie. not a 3rd party arrangement), 1706
isn't a problem, but some companies won't use sole proprietors.

Talk to an accountant or bookkeeper.

>
>How do you "collect" on finished projects?

Invoices are due upon receipt.  Don't wait until the project is
complete to bill.  Either work hourly and bill weekly or twice a
month, or if the price is fixed, then set up project "milestone" due
dates and assiociated payment dates.  All of my clients are large
companies, I haven't have collection problems, but others have.  What
I would probably do if it becomes obvious that I'm being stiffed, is
to follow up with delinquency letters with due dates and penalties to
apply if not paid.  Then contact a collection agency.

>
>Do you find it easy to get in OVER your head?
>
Sure!  Even after 10yrs of doing it!  But once you get things setup,
it's just a matter of routine.


Tim Oxler
TEO Computer Technologies Inc.
http://www.teo-computer.com
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Working from home questions (COBOL)

- **From:** "Donald Tees" <donald@willmack.com>

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Working from home questions (COBOL)

```

LOL! I think it is a great way to go, though you do have all
the added headaches of running a business - including don't
forget, ommissions and commissions insurance. 

I am seriously thinking about doing it fulltime myself,
as I like my customers and enjoy working for them more than
I do working for my company. On the other hand, the one BIG
drawback is lack of resources. It costs a pretty penny 
to pick up say, an AS/400 for use at your home office! 

-Paul


Tim Oxler (tim.oxler@NOSPAMteo-computer.com) wrote:
: "William R. Fink" <bfink@spam.apci.net> wrote:

: >I know this is off the subject of COBOL (sort of).
: >
: >I have been considering "Moonlighting" by working on COBOL programs during
: >my "OFF" hours.   Are there any of you who do this kind of thing?
: >

: Well, I've been telecommuting from my home for the past 3yrs.  I've
: also got someone "moonlighting" for me, and he does work from his
: home, as does another contractor who works for me full time.  But
: since I have to work with 2 other guys, who work different hours, it
: can turn into 10-12hr work days.
: http://www.teo-computer.com/dev/telecom.html

: >During the day, I am a web application programmer (no COBOL there) and would
: >like to keep my skills up in COBOL.  Primarily because I teach COBOL at the
: >Community College level and do not want to get too rusty.
: >
: >If any of you do this, can you answer a few of my questions?
: >

: Telecommuting part-time as a moonlighter is very very difficult to get
: hired for.  My moonlighter guy, has specific application skills that
: got him the work.  

: Perhaps Y2k work might be a possibility.

: But, I'd also look at COBOL/CGI and/or NetExpress considering your
: backround.

: >
: >How do you drum up business (other than word of mouth)?

: I've gotten my work through experience and reputation.  However, I
: also send out pocket calendars with my business name address info, and
: they have gotten me business.  It cost me $300, but netted me $10,000.

: >
: >Did you need the assistance of a lawyer?

: No, but a good bookkeeper or accountant helps alot.  When I got
: started, I kept my previous sub-contract agreements, got blacked out
: copies of contracts from other contractors, and Quicken Lawyer
: (originally I used It's Legal).  I make my own contracts.  And with
: high grade paper and company logo, you'd think a lawyer drew it up.

: BTW, I decided to go this route and bypass the use of a lawyer because
: of the no more than 20 minutes of work a lawyer spent on me when I
: incorporated 10yrs ago for $500.  All she did was fill out a
: "fill-in-the-blank" incorporation form, put it in a fancy binder, and
: call the state and register the corporation name.  Quicken Lawyer will
: do much of the same for contracts.

: However, if I was in business with others, I'd use a lawyer.

: If you do use a lawyer, accountant and/or bookkeeper, don't use the
: yellowpages to find one.  Get one, based on referrals.

: >
: >What TAX considerations did you need to make?

: For moonlighting, 1099 (or more accurately, sole proprietor) work is
: probably the easiest to get started.  But, I'd never hire you as a
: sole proprietor to do work for a client of mine, because of Section
: 1706.  I'd hire you as W2, unless you would incorporate.  If you work
: direct to a company/client (ie. not a 3rd party arrangement), 1706
: isn't a problem, but some companies won't use sole proprietors.

: Talk to an accountant or bookkeeper.

: >
: >How do you "collect" on finished projects?

: Invoices are due upon receipt.  Don't wait until the project is
: complete to bill.  Either work hourly and bill weekly or twice a
: month, or if the price is fixed, then set up project "milestone" due
: dates and assiociated payment dates.  All of my clients are large
: companies, I haven't have collection problems, but others have.  What
: I would probably do if it becomes obvious that I'm being stiffed, is
: to follow up with delinquency letters with due dates and penalties to
: apply if not paid.  Then contact a collection agency.

: >
: >Do you find it easy to get in OVER your head?
: >
: Sure!  Even after 10yrs of doing it!  But once you get things setup,
: it's just a matter of routine.


: Tim Oxler
: TEO Computer Technologies Inc.
: http://www.teo-computer.com
```

paulr@bix.com (paulr) wrote:

[snip]
>
>I am seriously thinking about doing it fulltime myself,
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
>-Paul
[snip]

You don't have to buy or lease an AS/400.  Your PC can act as a remote
terminal if you have the right comminication software, and your client
has remote connection capabilities.

Even today's MVS for mainframes have TCP/IP connections.

Products like Shiva, allows connection to client/servers and putting
the servers disk directories within access on your Win95 Explorer.

Products like Rumba and SimPC connect to mainframe TSO and CICS.  And
they are very stable.

Almost all of my connections are in other states and cities, and all
are either via the internet or 1-800-# phone call.


Tim Oxler
TEO Computer Technologies Inc.
http://www.teo-computer.com

You almost NEVER get burned with small companies- in fact, it is 
all too often the exact opposite. Some unscrupulous critter out 
there scoops someone for $30 to $40L for a job worth about $4-6K.
(*sigh*) 

I love working with smaller companies, even though it is often
a challenge. (I have one customer now who is THE perfect customer
to work for- he understands a LOT about the systems and knows
pretty much exactly what he wants.) 

It's those medium sized or large companies that always try to 
screw with you. That's true even in W2 work!I pumpu out about 90
hours per week at my W2 these days, and it isn't as much fun
as the 10 to 20 I squeeze out moonlighting. :) 

-Paul

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: I'm confused!

- **From:** "Donald Tees" <donald@willmack.com>
- **Date:** 1998-07-09T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol

- **References:** `<35A3A5E3.26F935E7@lnotes3.BankofNY.com> <1998070905034700.BAA06350@ladder01.news.aol.com>`

```
>That is different as only one mechanic works on a car while a team of
>programmer (inexperienced/experienced) work together to develop a programm.
>Then, a group of tester check and recheck  the program before the program
comes
>to the end-user..

Boy are you dreaming.  The second programmer is put onto the team
when the number of programs passes fifty or so.  A "group" of testers?
There are a few projects like that. About one in ten thousand.

The way it works is like this.  A one man year  program equals
one programmer for a year, or two programmers for eight months, or
three programmers for six months, or four programmers for eight months
or five programmers for a year, or twenty programmers for two years.
```

## Thread: Static linking from DLLs — 19 msgs

### Static linking from DLLs

- **From:** "Leif Svalgaard" <leif@ibm.net>

```
Below is some correspondence re linking of DLLs that I have received.
It all started because I asked how to create a stand-alone EXE file with
Fujitsu Cobol. Now, F-Cobol comes with a bunch of DLLs. For distribution
purposes I would like to only distribute the single (albeit large EXE file)
rather than my small EXE and half a Meg of Fujitsu run-time DLLs (you
know the F3*.DLLs). My end users always end up losing some of these
(don't ask me how!). To create an EXE you link your OBJ statically with
modules from link libraries. So it stands to reason (how else?) that the
meat of the code in the DLLs must be put in link library. This was my
question: how to do that.

Now, after some run-around (like: a LIB is created when you (who? me?)
link the DDL: ain't mine to link) I got the following reply (it seems Thane
is
just as much in the dark as I am):

Replies:  (BTW, Fujitsu, I do appreciate your valiant efforts to educate us)

Fujitsu COBOL supports dynamic loading DLLs and also dynamic loading
multiple Entry Points in the DLL.  To dynamically call a DLL or Entry Point
in the DLL, use the DLOAD compiler directive.

Fujitsu COBOL V2 for Windows 3.1 (16-bit) includes Microsoft's 16-bit
IMPLIB.EXE utility.

For creating LIB files for Windows 95/NT (32-bit) see:
http://support.microsoft.com/support/kb/articles/q131/3/13.asp

I went to this site and found this:

Normally, when building a .DLL or any target that exports functions or data
items, an import library (and exports file) is generated as part of the
linking process. But in the case of a third-party .DLL that does not ship
with an import library, you may need to generate an import library in order
to use the .DLL successfully using load-time dynamic linking. An import
library is not needed for run-time dynamic linking.

There is nothing here about static linking. There is an ominous reference to
IMPORT libraries,
but I don't think you use import libraries for a static link(???).

There is More:

#### ↳ Re: Static linking from DLLs

- **From:** "Kevin J. Hansen" <screenio@pobox.alaska.net>
- **Date:** 1998-07-07T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<wMwo1.2$dl3.337730@binary.alaska.net>`
- **References:** `<35a24aac.0@news1.ibm.net>`

```
If I understand correctly, you wish to statically link the runtime code
contained in a DLL into your application, instead of shipping the DLL with
your application.

The short answer is:  You can't do it.

The entry points in a DLL are generally called statically by your program.
Your program gains access to these entry points by being linked with an
import library derived from the DLL.  In the 16-bit world, you could build
an import library using the utility IMPLIB.EXE.  In the 32-bit world, the
LINKer creates an import library automatically when the DLL is built.

The import library merely provides a mechanism that will, at runtime, load
the DLL when you call one of the entry points exported by the DLL, and pass
control to the DLL.  That's why import libraries are so small; they're just
pass-through code.  The real meat resides in the DLL.

There are a number of attractive points to using the DLL approach:

- Only one copy of the DLL is loaded into memory; the code may be used by
many applications.  Each application gets its own copy of the DLL's data
segment, so there are no conflicts or reentrancy problems.

- From the software vendor's point of view, you can (generally) distribute
bug fixes and upgrades in DLLs and not require that the developer re-LINK
the application; all your have to do is to replace the old DLL with the new
one and, Voila!  you're running the latest code.  It's much less trouble for
all concerned.

- For our ScreenIO application, we only need to maintain one version of the
software (in DLL form) that may be used by any 32-bit compiler.
Compatibility issues are addressed using simple COBOL stubs (compiled using
the target compiler) that are placed in the import library distributed with
the runtime DLL.

Of course, there are downsides...

- Your installation software has to be careful not to clobber newer versions
of DLLs by installing older versions over the top of them.

- If your application terminates abnormally, and you're testing code
contained in a DLL, you may have to reboot to (metaphorically speaking) kick
a loaded DLL out of memory in order to replace it.

But I digress...  Here's the bottom line:

If the software vendor provided an object library containing the runtime
routines to you, and you linked your application with that library (instead
of the import library), you would be able to bundle the whole application
into an EXE without the need to ship runtime DLLs.  If the vendor doesn't
provide the runtime routines to you in this form, you're going to have to
ship the vendor's runtime DLL files.
```

- **From:** "Donald Tees" <donald@willmack.com>

>In this case you can package all of your programs into a single EXE and
>install that EXE along with the Fujitsu COBOL DLLs into a unique
application
>specific disk directory.  In doing so you are isolating your application
>with the specific version and release of the Fujitsu COBOL Runtime System

I realize that this can be done, I am just not sure that I like it.  DLL's
by their
nature, are becoming one of the biggest headaches in the computer world.
It sounds great in theory, but what it boils down to is having to keep track
of every DLL on the system, where it is, and what is on every system at any
given time.

I manage about 300 computers.  At any given time, I could have several of
my systems, and several other pieces of software by other people on any
given system.  To complicate matters, any one of my systems could have
fourty or fifty Cobol programs.  What this approach means is that if I
change
one program, I really have to recompile and retest every program on the
system,  OR never upgrade my compiler, OR isolate every program into
it's own directory.

It would be a lot simpler to have a way of ensuring that every program
was/is
a complete, intact unit. That is precisely why the data processing world has
both static and dynamic linking. Mind you, DLL methodology may have it's
place, but I am not sure that it should be the ONLY way. The exact same
problem
exist with nearly every piece of Microsoft software, and is one of the main
reasons
that Windows 95 has such a flakey reputation.  Every install one does on
autopilot updates dozens of programs.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Static linking from DLLs

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** "Kevin G. Rhoads" <T_Rhoads@NoSpam.CLASSIC.MSN.COM>
- **Date:** 1998-07-10T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<01bdac68$099b7080$LocalHost@stupidwin95>`
- **References:** `<35a24aac.0@news1.ibm.net> <wMwo1.2$dl3.337730@binary.alaska.net> <6nun82$sjd$1@news.igs.net> <6o03gn$1ro$1@nntp2.ba.best.com>`

```
Actually, even in that case it is a crap-shoot.

If some other program on the machine in question was
compiled using any of the DLLs in question, (e.g.,
another Fujitsu Cobol generated EXE), and
if that other program is already running --
THEN any of the DLLs in question may already
be loaded.  

The OS will not use the DLL from the same directory,
if it is already active in memory when the application is
invoked.

As long as you use DLLs you are exposed to the versioning
problem, and there is NO way to be certain to avoid it.

You can have your application call the DLL unload entries
in Windows to force and preloaded DLLs to unload, but you can't
be sure that some other application will load it after you've forced it
out and before you can load your own copy.   Highly unlikely?  
Maybe.  Certain?  Absolutely not!

Static linking has real advantages and should not be arbitrarily 
eliminated.

Now Fujistsu has the RTL source.  They've already compiled
and/or assembled it in order to link DLL versions of the RTL.

All they need do is take the same object files that go into
XYZ.DLL and LIB them all together as XYZ_static.LIB. 
It is actually easier to generate a LIB than  DLL. 

This is NOT rocket science.  
```

While I am not much of a Windows programmer,
I can tell you you are absolutely correct.

After all, that was one of the prime benefits 
trumpeted for DLLs -- only one copy of the
code would be resident at any one time.

If the DLL is already loaded, then the OS will
NOT load another copy.  

If you try to force out the pre-loaded DLL,
aside from possibly breaking the other app.'s
invocation, you are still not certain to get your
version of the DLL.  The other app. or a third one
could load a different version of the DLL in question
after you've unloaded it and before you can load  your
preferred version.

There is NO certainty with DLLs but one:  And that
one is that there is NO certainty with DLLs.  (Is it
any wonder any competent programmer has headaches
dealing with DLLs?)

```
It gets worse.  The thing that has not been mentioned yet, is
that each DLL can call other DLLs.  Even if I put every Fujitsu
DLL in my directory, I cannot be sure that each one does not
point to dozens of other DLL's by other vendors. The only real
recourse is to put every single DLL on the system into each
directory, each and every time you do a software install.  I found
that out the hard way this weekend.

Let me tell you what happened.

First, I put a new network card into my system, as I had to
free up an old style slot.  I took out my NE2000, and installed
a PCI card.  Five applications crashed. It seems that a DLL
replaced pointed to a common one that the new driver upgraded.

Fifteen hours later, I ended up doing a complete restore from tape,
as I could not get everything working at once for love nor money. I then
deleted every device, turned off plug and play, and put things back
one at a time until I got all working.  It seems that one device would
only work with one specific old DLL, and another would only work
with one specific new DLL.  The applications required the old
DLL.  The applications were my mail, my word processor,
and my spreadsheet.  I shudder to think if it were a payroll system.

There is also the fact that I do backup to tape each and every night.
How many do?  Most of my customers do not, even though I jump
up and down, and tear out my hair at the fact. I even have a postal
meter that prints "have you done your backup today?" on each and
every invoice that goes out the door.

If I had not had backup, I would not be posting this.

This is the crux of the matter. If what you ship is a large application, I
agree
that you are MUCH better off going with DLLs. If, on the other hand, you are
also (or solely, as the case may be) shipping a single useful TOOL or
utility,
you would like to simply ship an all-encompassing EXE file. The point is
that you would like to have the CHOICE. This whole thread is about making
it clear to Fujitsu that they could IMPROVE their product immensely by
giving developers that choice. So, what we need is an object library with
the runtime routines as well as the DLLs. How about it, Fujitsu?

Leif Svalgaard <leif@ibm.net> wrote in article
<35a2a8a9.0@news1.ibm.net>...

> Kevin J. Hansen wrote in message ...
> >If I understand correctly, you wish to statically link the runtime code

> >routines to you, and you linked your application with that library
(instead
> >of the import library), you would be able to bundle the whole
application
> >into an EXE without the need to ship runtime DLLs.  If the vendor
doesn't
> >provide the runtime routines to you in this form, you're going to have
to
> >ship the vendor's runtime DLL files.
> 
> 
> This is the crux of the matter. If what you ship is a large application,
I
> agree
> that you are MUCH better off going with DLLs. If, on the other hand, you
are
> also (or solely, as the case may be) shipping a single useful TOOL or
> utility,
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
> 

Leif, 

It is possible to create static executables (both EXEs and DLLs) ie modules
with the run-time code built in, with Micro Focus NetExpress (see
http://www.microfocus.com). The option to create modules that use the
run-time as a DLL is also available as this is preferable where an
application consists of more than one executable module. So, you do have
the choice.

In a separate reply to your note, a comment was made about use of DLLs
potentially causing problems when upgrades occur. However, both Windows 95
and NT will attempt to load DLLs from the application directory in
preference to system directory etc. Therefore if DLLs required by an
application are placed in the same directory as the application this
problem should not occur. 

> 
> 
>
```

## Thread: Random Number Generator — 6 msgs

### Random Number Generator

- **From:** rdavis@ozemail.com.au (Ron Davis)
- **Date:** 1998-07-08T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<rdavis.63.001BF99D@ozemail.com.au>`

```
Hi all,
I need a random number generator, (rough and ready will do, only for test data 
generation) that  I can run under Cobol 2 on an MVS platform. Source code 
preferrred, either COBOL or Assembler.  (I know one is available in the 
Language Environment but we don't run it!).
If you can help please reply by email to:
rdavis@ozemail.com.au or
ron.davis@dva.gov.au
Thanks
Ron Davis
```

#### ↳ Re: Random Number Generator

- **From:** "WOB" <wobconsult@sprynet.com>
- **Date:** 1998-07-07T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<6nuen4$dc3$1@juliana.sprynet.com>`
- **References:** `<rdavis.63.001BF99D@ozemail.com.au>`

```
One way would be to call an ASSEMBLER Sub-Program, which would pass back a
doubleword-binary (PIC S9(18) BINARY) value to the COBOL Program containing
the results of a STCK (Store-Clock) instruction. The caller can then
manipulate the value using different methods (such as date, time, etc) to
arrive at a random-number.

STORCLK    CSECT
                    STM          14,12,12(13)        SAVE REGISTERS
                    USING       *,15                     R15 IS
BASE-REGISTER
                    L               1,0(,1)                  PARAMETER
ADDRESSABILITY
                    STCK        0(1)                      ISSUE A
'STORE-CLOCK'
                    LM            14,12,12(13)         RESTORE REGISTERS
                    XR            15,15                    MAKE COBOL HAPPY
                    BR            14                         RETURN TO THE
CALLER
                    END

    BTW, the results of a STCK instruction turns over around Sept 2042 and
will not be in compliance. Get ready for the Y2K+42 crisis! Save it for your
grandchildren....

Cheers,

WOB,
Atlanta

Ron, I'm sending you the code by e-mail, but I thought that maybe there is a
wider
audience for this kind of routine, so I'm posting it here as well. You can
use MATHPK
as it is, or cut the random code out.


000100 IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.
000200 PROGRAM-ID.    MATHPK.
000300
000400 AUTHOR.        LEIF SVALGAARD.
000500 DATE-WRITTEN.  87/02/01
000600     -REVISED:  93/08/20.
000700
000800 ENVIRONMENT DIVISION.
000900
001000 CONFIGURATION SECTION.
001100 SOURCE-COMPUTER. PORTABLE.
001200 OBJECT-COMPUTER. PORTABLE.
001300
001400 DATA DIVISION.
001500
001600 WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
001700
001800 01  HIGH-PRECISION-CONSTANTS.

002000                                              VALUE +0.000000000.
002100     02  VALUE-TEN               PIC S9(9)V9(9) COMP
002200                                              VALUE +10.00000000.

002900

020300 LINKAGE SECTION.
020400
020500 01  MATHPK-CONTROL.
020600     02  SESSION-TASK-ID         PIC X(4).
020700     02  MATHPK-OPERATION        PIC X(8).
020800     02  MATHPK-FEEDBACK         PIC X.
020900         88  MATHPK-DOMAIN-ERROR            VALUE IS "D".
021000         88  MATHPK-RANGE-ERROR             VALUE IS "R".
021100
021200     02  MATHPK-RESULT           PIC S9(9)V9(9) COMP.
021300     02  MATHPK-ARGUMENT-1       PIC S9(9)V9(9) COMP.
021400     02  MATHPK-ARGUMENT-2       PIC S9(9)V9(9) COMP.
021500
021600 PROCEDURE DIVISION
021700     USING MATHPK-CONTROL.
021800
021900 BEGIN-OF-PACKAGE.
022000     MOVE SPACE TO MATHPK-FEEDBACK
022100
022200     IF MATHPK-OPERATION = "SQRT"
022300         PERFORM SQRT-FUNCTION
022400     ELSE
022500     IF MATHPK-OPERATION = "POWER"
022600         PERFORM POWER-FUNCTION
022700     ELSE
022800     IF MATHPK-OPERATION = "LOG10"
022900         PERFORM LOGARITHM-10-FUNCTION
023000     ELSE
023100     IF MATHPK-OPERATION = "ALOG10"
023200         PERFORM ANTILOG-10-FUNCTION
023300     ELSE
023400     IF MATHPK-OPERATION = "ARCTAN"
023500         PERFORM ARCTAN-FUNCTION
023600     ELSE
023700     IF MATHPK-OPERATION = "SIN"
023800         PERFORM SINE-FUNCTION
023900     ELSE
024000     IF MATHPK-OPERATION = "COS"
024100         PERFORM COSINE-FUNCTION
024200     ELSE
024300     IF MATHPK-OPERATION = "ARCSIN"
024400         PERFORM ARCSINE-FUNCTION
024500     ELSE
024600     IF MATHPK-OPERATION = "EXP"
024700         PERFORM EXPONENTIAL-FUNCTION
024800     ELSE
024900     IF MATHPK-OPERATION = "RANDOM"
025000         PERFORM RANDOM-FUNCTION
025100     ELSE
025200     IF MATHPK-OPERATION = "SEEDRAND"
025300         PERFORM SEED-RANDOM-FUNCTION
025400     ELSE
025500     IF MATHPK-OPERATION = "E"
025600         PERFORM RETURN-VALUE-OF-E
025700     ELSE
025800     IF MATHPK-OPERATION = "PI"
025900         PERFORM RETURN-VALUE-OF-PI
026000     ELSE
026100     IF MATHPK-OPERATION = "GOLDEN"
026200         PERFORM RETURN-VALUE-OF-GOLDEN-RATIO
026300     ELSE
026400         MOVE "OP ERROR" TO MATHPK-FEEDBACK
026500     .
026600 RETURN-TO-CALLER.
026700     EXIT PROGRAM
026800     .
026900
027000***********************    SQUARE ROOT    ************************
027100*                                                                *
027200*               COMPUTES RESULT = SQRT (ARGUMENT-1)              *
027300*                                                                *
027400*----------------------------------------------------------------*
027500
027600 SQRT-FUNCTION.
027700     MOVE MATHPK-ARGUMENT-1 TO ARG-X
027800     PERFORM COMPUTE-SQRT-FUNCTION
027900     MOVE SQRT-X TO MATHPK-RESULT
028000     .
028100
028200 COMPUTE-SQRT-FUNCTION.
028300     IF ARG-X > ZERO
028400         PERFORM COMPUTE-SQRT-APPROX
028500     ELSE
028600     IF ARG-X < ZERO
028700         PERFORM SET-DOMAIN-ERROR
028800     ELSE
028900         MOVE ZERO TO SQRT-X
029000     .
029100
029200 COMPUTE-SQRT-APPROX.
029300     MOVE VALUE-ONE TO ITERATED-ARG
029400     IF ARG-X > VALUE-ONE
029500         COMPUTE ARG-LIMIT = ARG-X / 10
029600         MOVE SQRT-OF-5-POINT-5 TO SQRT-X
029700         PERFORM INCREASE-ARG-AND-ROOT
029800           UNTIL ITERATED-ARG > ARG-LIMIT
029900         PERFORM NEWTON-ITERATION 5 TIMES
030000     ELSE
030100     IF ARG-X < VALUE-ONE
030200         COMPUTE ARG-LIMIT = ARG-X * 10
030300         MOVE SQRT-OF-0-POINT-55 TO SQRT-X
030400         PERFORM DECREASE-ARG-AND-ROOT
030500           UNTIL ITERATED-ARG < ARG-LIMIT
030600         PERFORM NEWTON-ITERATION 5 TIMES
030700     ELSE
030800         MOVE VALUE-ONE TO SQRT-X
030900     .
031000
031100 INCREASE-ARG-AND-ROOT.
031200     COMPUTE ITERATED-ARG = ITERATED-ARG * VALUE-TEN
031300     COMPUTE SQRT-X = SQRT-X * SQRT-TEN
031400     .
031500
031600 DECREASE-ARG-AND-ROOT.
031700     COMPUTE ITERATED-ARG = ITERATED-ARG / VALUE-TEN
031800     COMPUTE SQRT-X = SQRT-X / SQRT-TEN
031900     .
032000
032100 NEWTON-ITERATION.
032200     COMPUTE SQRT-X = (ARG-X / SQRT-X + SQRT-X) / VALUE-TWO
032300     .
032400
032500 SET-DOMAIN-ERROR.
032600     MOVE "DOMAIN ERROR" TO MATHPK-FEEDBACK
032700     .
032800
032900********************     POWER FUNCTION     **********************
033000*                                                                *
033100*           COMPUTES RESULT = ARGUMENT-1 ** ARGUMENT-2           *
033200*                                                                *
033300*----------------------------------------------------------------*
033400
033500 POWER-FUNCTION.
033600     MOVE MATHPK-ARGUMENT-1 TO WORK-X
033700     MOVE MATHPK-ARGUMENT-2 TO EXPONENT-P
033800
033900     IF EXPONENT-P = ZERO
034000         MOVE VALUE-ONE TO MATHPK-RESULT
034100     ELSE
034200         IF WORK-X = ZERO
034300             IF EXPONENT-P > ZERO
034400                 MOVE ZERO TO MATHPK-RESULT
034500             ELSE
034600                 PERFORM SET-DOMAIN-ERROR
034700         ELSE
034800         IF WORK-X > ZERO
034900             PERFORM COMPUTE-POWER-FUNCTION
035000         ELSE
035100             PERFORM SET-DOMAIN-ERROR
035200     .
035300
035400 COMPUTE-POWER-FUNCTION.
035500     PERFORM COMPUTE-LOGARITHM-FUNCTION
035600     COMPUTE WORK-X ROUNDED = EXPONENT-P * LOGARITHM-X
035700
035800     IF WORK-X < TOP-LOGARITHM
035900         PERFORM COMPUTE-ANTILOG-FUNCTION
036000         MOVE  ANTILOG-X  TO MATHPK-RESULT
036100     ELSE
036200         PERFORM SET-RANGE-ERROR
036300     .
036400
036500 SET-RANGE-ERROR.
036600     MOVE "RANGE ERROR" TO MATHPK-FEEDBACK
036700     .
036800
036900******************    LOGARITHM 10 FUNCTION    *******************
037000*                                                                *
037100*              COMPUTES RESULT = LOG10 (ARGUMENT-1)              *
037200*                                                                *
037300*----------------------------------------------------------------*
037400
037500 LOGARITHM-10-FUNCTION.
037600     MOVE MATHPK-ARGUMENT-1 TO WORK-X
037700
037800     IF WORK-X > ZERO
037900         PERFORM COMPUTE-LOGARITHM-FUNCTION
038000         MOVE LOGARITHM-X TO MATHPK-RESULT
038100     ELSE
038200         PERFORM SET-DOMAIN-ERROR
038300     .
038400
038500 COMPUTE-LOGARITHM-FUNCTION.
038600     IF WORK-X < VALUE-ONE
038700         MOVE "NEG" TO SIGN-OF-LOGARITHM
038800         COMPUTE WORK-X = VALUE-ONE / WORK-X
038900     ELSE
039000         MOVE "POS" TO SIGN-OF-LOGARITHM
039100     .
039200     PERFORM REDUCE-X-TO-INTERVAL--1-TO-2
039300     PERFORM RATIONAL-LOG-TRANSFORMATION
039400     PERFORM EVALUATE-LOGARITHM-APPROX
039500
039600     IF LOG-IS-NEGATIVE
039700         COMPUTE LOGARITHM-X = VALUE-ZERO - LOGARITHM-X
039800     .
039900
040000 REDUCE-X-TO-INTERVAL--1-TO-2.
040100     MOVE ZERO TO CHARACTERISTIC-X
040200     PERFORM DIVIDE-BY-TWO
040300       UNTIL WORK-X < VALUE-TWO
040400     .
040500
040600 DIVIDE-BY-TWO.
040700     COMPUTE WORK-X = WORK-X / VALUE-TWO
040800     ADD VALUE-ONE TO CHARACTERISTIC-X
040900     .
041000
041100 RATIONAL-LOG-TRANSFORMATION.
041200     COMPUTE TRANSF--X = (WORK-X - SQRT-TWO)
041300                       / (WORK-X + SQRT-TWO)
041400     COMPUTE TRANSF-XX = TRANSF--X * TRANSF--X
041500     .
041600
041700 EVALUATE-LOGARITHM-APPROX.
041800     COMPUTE MANTISSA-X = ONE-HALF + TRANSF--X * (LOG-COEFF1
041900                                   + TRANSF-XX * (LOG-COEFF3
042000                                   + TRANSF-XX * (LOG-COEFF5
042100                                   + TRANSF-XX *  LOG-COEFF7
042200                                                         )))
042300     COMPUTE LOGARITHM-X ROUNDED = (MANTISSA-X + CHARACTERISTIC-X)
042400                                         / LOG2-OF-TEN
042500     .
042600
042700*******************    ANTILOG 10 FUNCTION    ********************
042800*                                                                *
042900*            COMPUTES RESULT = ANTILOG10 (ARGUMENT-1)            *
043000*                                                                *
043100*----------------------------------------------------------------*
043200
043300 ANTILOG-10-FUNCTION.
043400     MOVE MATHPK-ARGUMENT-1 TO WORK-X
043500     PERFORM COMPUTE-ANTILOG-FUNCTION
043600     MOVE ANTILOG-X TO MATHPK-RESULT
043700     .
043800
043900 COMPUTE-ANTILOG-FUNCTION.
044000     IF WORK-X < ZERO
044100         MOVE "NEG" TO SIGN-OF-LOGARITHM
044200         COMPUTE TRANSF--X = VALUE-ZERO - WORK-X
044300     ELSE
044400         MOVE "POS" TO SIGN-OF-LOGARITHM
044500         COMPUTE TRANSF--X =   WORK-X
044600     .
044700     IF TRANSF--X < TOP-LOGARITHM
044800         PERFORM COMPUTE-RESULT-IN-RANGE
044900     ELSE
045000         PERFORM SET-RANGE-ERROR
045100     .
045200
045300 COMPUTE-RESULT-IN-RANGE.
045400     MOVE ZERO TO CHARACTERISTIC-X
045500     PERFORM SUBTRACT-ONE
045600       UNTIL TRANSF--X < VALUE-ONE
045700
045800     PERFORM EVALUATE-ANTILOG-APPROX
045900     MOVE TRANSF-XX TO WORK-X
046000
046100     PERFORM MULTIPLY-BY-TEN
046200       UNTIL CHARACTERISTIC-X < VALUE-ONE
046300
046400     IF LOG-IS-NEGATIVE
046500         COMPUTE ANTILOG-X ROUNDED = VALUE-ONE / WORK-X
046600     ELSE
046700         COMPUTE ANTILOG-X ROUNDED = WORK-X
046800     .
046900
047000 SUBTRACT-ONE.
047100     SUBTRACT VALUE-ONE FROM TRANSF--X
047200     ADD      VALUE-ONE TO   CHARACTERISTIC-X
047300     .
047400
047500 EVALUATE-ANTILOG-APPROX.
047600     COMPUTE TRANSF--W =             TRANSF--X * (ALOG-KOEFF5
047700                                   + TRANSF--X * (ALOG-KOEFF6
047800                                   + TRANSF--X *  ALOG-KOEFF7))
047900     COMPUTE TRANSF--X = VALUE-ONE + TRANSF--X * (ALOG-KOEFF1
048000                                   + TRANSF--X * (ALOG-KOEFF2
048100                                   + TRANSF--X * (ALOG-KOEFF3
048200                                   + TRANSF--X * (ALOG-KOEFF4
048300                                   + TRANSF--W))))
048400     COMPUTE TRANSF-XX ROUNDED = TRANSF--X * TRANSF--X
048500     .
048600
048700 MULTIPLY-BY-TEN.
048800     COMPUTE WORK-X = WORK-X * VALUE-TEN
048900     SUBTRACT VALUE-ONE FROM CHARACTERISTIC-X
049000     .
049100
049200*********************    ARCTAN FUNCTION    **********************
049300*                                                                *
049400*              COMPUTES RESULT = ARCTAN (ARGUMENT-1)             *
049500*                                                                *
049600*----------------------------------------------------------------*
049700
049800 ARCTAN-FUNCTION.
049900     MOVE MATHPK-ARGUMENT-1 TO WORK-X
050000     PERFORM COMPUTE-ARCTAN-FUNCTION
050100     MOVE ARCTAN-X TO MATHPK-RESULT
050200     .
050300
050400 COMPUTE-ARCTAN-FUNCTION.
050500     IF WORK-X < ZERO
050600         COMPUTE WORK-X = VALUE-ZERO - WORK-X
050700         MOVE "NEG" TO SIGN-OF-ARGUMENT
050800         PERFORM COMPUTE-ARCTAN-APPROX
050900     ELSE
051000     IF WORK-X > ZERO
051100         MOVE "POS" TO SIGN-OF-ARGUMENT
051200         PERFORM COMPUTE-ARCTAN-APPROX
051300     ELSE
051400         MOVE ZERO  TO ARCTAN-X
051500     .
051600
051700 COMPUTE-ARCTAN-APPROX.
051800     PERFORM RATIONAL-TAN-TRANSFORMATION
051900     PERFORM EVALUATE-ARCTAN-APPROX
052000     IF ARGUMENT-IS-NEGATIVE
052100         COMPUTE ARCTAN-X = VALUE-ZERO - ARCTAN-X
052200     .
052300
052400 RATIONAL-TAN-TRANSFORMATION.
052500     COMPUTE TRANSF--X = (WORK-X - VALUE-ONE)
052600                       / (WORK-X + VALUE-ONE)
052700     COMPUTE TRANSF-XX = TRANSF--X * TRANSF--X
052800     .
052900
053000 EVALUATE-ARCTAN-APPROX.
053100     COMPUTE WORK-W = TRANSF-XX * (ATAN-COEFF9
053200                    + TRANSF-XX * (ATAN-COEFF11
053300                    + TRANSF-XX * (ATAN-COEFF13
053400                    + TRANSF-XX *  ATAN-COEFF15)))
053500     COMPUTE WORK-X = TRANSF--X * (ATAN-COEFF1
053600                    + TRANSF-XX * (ATAN-COEFF3
053700                    + TRANSF-XX * (ATAN-COEFF5
053800                    + TRANSF-XX * (ATAN-COEFF7
053900                    + WORK-W))))
054000     COMPUTE ARCTAN-X = PI-QUARTER + WORK-X
054100     .
054200
054300*********************    ARCSIN FUNCTION    **********************
054400*                                                                *
054500*              COMPUTES RESULT = ARCSIN (ARGUMENT-1)             *
054600*                                                                *
054700*----------------------------------------------------------------*
054800
054900 ARCSINE-FUNCTION.
055000     MOVE MATHPK-ARGUMENT-1 TO ARG-X
055100     IF ARG-X < ZERO
055200         MOVE "NEGATIVE" TO SIGN-OF-ARGUMENT
055300         COMPUTE ARG-X = VALUE-ZERO - ARG-X
055400     ELSE
055500         MOVE "POSITIVE" TO SIGN-OF-ARGUMENT
055600     .
055700     IF ARG-X > VALUE-ONE
055800         PERFORM SET-DOMAIN-ERROR
055900     ELSE
056000     IF ARG-X < +0.0001
056100         MOVE ARG-X TO ARCSIN-X
056200     ELSE
056300         PERFORM COMPUTE-ARCSIN-APPROX
056400     .
056500     IF ARGUMENT-IS-NEGATIVE
056600         COMPUTE MATHPK-RESULT = VALUE-ZERO - ARCSIN-X
056700     ELSE
056800         COMPUTE MATHPK-RESULT =   ARCSIN-X
056900     .
057000
057100 COMPUTE-ARCSIN-APPROX.
057200     MOVE ARG-X TO X1
057300     COMPUTE ARG-X = VALUE-ONE - ARG-X
057400     PERFORM COMPUTE-SQRT-FUNCTION
057500
057600     COMPUTE TRANSF--W =          (ARCSIN-COEFF3 + X1
057700                                * (ARCSIN-COEFF4 + X1
057800                                * (ARCSIN-COEFF5 + X1
057900                                * (ARCSIN-COEFF6 + X1
058000                                *  ARCSIN-COEFF7))))
058100     COMPUTE ARCSIN-X = PI-HALF - SQRT-X
058200                                * (ARCSIN-COEFF0 + X1
058300                                * (ARCSIN-COEFF1 + X1
058400                                * (ARCSIN-COEFF2 + X1
058500                                *  TRANSF--W)))
058600     .
058700
058800*********************    COSINE FUNCTION    **********************
058900*                                                                *
059000*               COMPUTES RESULT = COS (ARGUMENT-1)               *
059100*                                                                *
059200*----------------------------------------------------------------*
059300
059400 COSINE-FUNCTION.
059500     COMPUTE ARG-X = PI-HALF - MATHPK-ARGUMENT-1
059600     PERFORM COMPUTE-SINE-FUNCTION
059700     MOVE SINE-X TO MATHPK-RESULT
059800     .
059900
060000**********************    SINE FUNCTION    ***********************
060100*                                                                *
060200*               COMPUTES RESULT = SIN (ARGUMENT-1)               *
060300*                                                                *
060400*----------------------------------------------------------------*
060500
060600 SINE-FUNCTION.
060700     COMPUTE ARG-X = MATHPK-ARGUMENT-1
060800     PERFORM COMPUTE-SINE-FUNCTION
060900     MOVE SINE-X TO MATHPK-RESULT
061000     .
061100
061200 COMPUTE-SINE-FUNCTION.
061300     IF ARG-X < ZERO
061400         MOVE "NEGATIVE" TO SIGN-OF-ARGUMENT
061500         COMPUTE ARG-X = VALUE-ZERO - ARG-X
061600     ELSE
061700         MOVE "POSITIVE" TO SIGN-OF-ARGUMENT
061800     .
061900     IF ARG-X > TWO-PI
062000         PERFORM REDUCE-TO-WITHIN-TWO-PI
062100     ELSE
062200         MOVE ARG-X TO X1
062300     .
062400     IF X1 > VALUE-PI
062500         SUBTRACT VALUE-PI FROM X1
062600         MOVE "NEGATIVE" TO SIGN-OF-RESULT
062700     ELSE
062800         MOVE "POSITIVE" TO SIGN-OF-RESULT
062900     .
063000     IF X1 > PI-HALF
063100         COMPUTE X1 = VALUE-PI - X1
063200     .
063300     PERFORM COMPUTE-SINE-APPROX
063400
063500     IF RESULT-IS-NEGATIVE
063600         COMPUTE SINE-X = VALUE-ZERO - SINE-X
063700     .
063800     IF ARGUMENT-IS-NEGATIVE
063900         COMPUTE SINE-X = VALUE-ZERO - SINE-X
064000     .
064100
064200 REDUCE-TO-WITHIN-TWO-PI.
064300     COMPUTE NUMBER-OF-TURNS ROUNDED = ARG-X / TWO-PI
064400
064500     COMPUTE FRACTIONAL-TURN  = NUMBER-OF-TURNS - WHOLE-TURNS
064600     COMPUTE       X1         = FRACTIONAL-TURN * TWO-PI
064700     .
064800
064900 COMPUTE-SINE-APPROX.
065000     IF X1 < +0.0001
065100         MOVE X1 TO SINE-X
065200     ELSE
065300         COMPUTE X1 = X1 / PI-HALF
065400         COMPUTE X2 = X1 * X1
065500         COMPUTE SINE-X = X1 * (SINE-COEFF1
065600                        + X2 * (SINE-COEFF3
065700                        + X2 * (SINE-COEFF5
065800                        + X2 * (SINE-COEFF7
065900                        + X2 *  SINE-COEFF9))))
066000
066100         IF SINE-X > VALUE-ONE
066200             MOVE VALUE-ONE TO SINE-X
066300     .
066400
066500*******************   EXPONENTIAL FUNCTION    ********************
066600*                                                                *
066700*               COMPUTES RESULT = EXP (ARGUMENT-1)               *
066800*                                                                *
066900*----------------------------------------------------------------*
067000
067100 EXPONENTIAL-FUNCTION.
067200     MOVE MATHPK-ARGUMENT-1 TO ARG-X
067300     IF ARG-X < ZERO
067400         MOVE "NEGATIVE" TO SIGN-OF-ARGUMENT
067500         IF ARG-X < -21.5
067600             MOVE ZEROES TO EXP-X
067700         ELSE
067800             COMPUTE ARG-X = VALUE-ZERO - ARG-X
067900             PERFORM COMPUTE-EXP-APPROX
068000     ELSE
068100     IF ARG-X > ZERO
068200         MOVE "POSITIVE" TO SIGN-OF-ARGUMENT
068300         IF ARG-X > +20.6
068400             PERFORM SET-RANGE-ERROR
068500         ELSE
068600             PERFORM COMPUTE-EXP-APPROX
068700     ELSE
068800         MOVE VALUE-ONE TO EXP-X
068900     .
069000     MOVE EXP-X TO MATHPK-RESULT
069100     .
069200
069300 COMPUTE-EXP-APPROX.
069400     COMPUTE WORK-W =     ARG-X * (EXP-COEFF4
069500                        + ARG-X * (EXP-COEFF5
069600                        + ARG-X *  EXP-COEFF6))
069700     COMPUTE ARG-X  = 1 + ARG-X * (EXP-COEFF1
069800                        + ARG-X * (EXP-COEFF2
069900                        + ARG-X * (EXP-COEFF3
070000                        + WORK-W)))
070100
070200     COMPUTE EXP-X = ARG-X * ARG-X
070300     COMPUTE EXP-X = EXP-X * EXP-X
070400
070500     IF ARGUMENT-IS-NEGATIVE
070600         COMPUTE EXP-X = VALUE-ONE / EXP-X
070700     .
070800
070900**********************   RANDOM FUNCTION    **********************
071000*                                                                *
071100*            COMPUTES RESULT = RANDOM FRACTION IN (0:1)          *
071200*                                                                *
071300*----------------------------------------------------------------*
071400
071500 RANDOM-FUNCTION.
071600     MOVE MATHPK-ARGUMENT-1 TO RANDOM-INTEGER
071700
071800     COMPUTE RANDOM-PRODUCT  = RANDOM-INCREMENT
071900                             + RANDOM-MULTIPLIER * RANDOM-INTEGER
072000     COMPUTE RANDOM-QUOTIENT = RANDOM-PRODUCT    / RANDOM-MODULUS
072100     COMPUTE RANDOM-INTEGER  = RANDOM-PRODUCT
072200                             - RANDOM-QUOTIENT   * RANDOM-MODULUS
072300     COMPUTE MATHPK-RESULT   = RANDOM-INTEGER    / RANDOM-ADJUST
072400
072500     MOVE RANDOM-INTEGER TO MATHPK-ARGUMENT-1
072600     .
072700
072800*******************    SEED RANDOM FUNCTION    *******************
072900*                                                                *
073000*            SEEDS THE RANDOM NUMBER GENERATOR WITH THE          *
073100*            NUMBER IN ARGUMENT-1, WHICH MUST BE WITHIN          *
073200*                       THE INTERVAL (0:1)                       *
073300*                                                                *
073400*----------------------------------------------------------------*
073500
073600 SEED-RANDOM-FUNCTION.
073700     MOVE MATHPK-ARGUMENT-1 TO ARG-X
073800     IF ZERO < ARG-X
073900        AND    ARG-X < VALUE-ONE
074000         COMPUTE RANDOM-INTEGER = ARG-X * RANDOM-PRECISION
074100         MOVE RANDOM-INTEGER TO MATHPK-ARGUMENT-1
074200     ELSE
074300         PERFORM SET-DOMAIN-ERROR
074400     .
074500
074600***********************    VALUE OF E    *************************
074700*                                                                *
074800*             RETURNS RESULT = VALUE OF E = 2.718...             *
074900*                                                                *
075000*----------------------------------------------------------------*
075100
075200 RETURN-VALUE-OF-E.
075300     MOVE VALUE-E TO MATHPK-RESULT
075400     .
075500
075600**********************    VALUE OF PI    *************************
075700*                                                                *
075800*            RETURNS RESULT = VALUE OF PI = 3.141...             *
075900*                                                                *
076000*----------------------------------------------------------------*
076100
076200 RETURN-VALUE-OF-PI.
076300     MOVE VALUE-PI TO MATHPK-RESULT
076400     .
076500
076600******************    VALUE OF GOLDEN RATIO    *******************
076700*                                                                *
076800*       RETURNS RESULT = VALUE OF GOLDEN RATIO = 1.618...        *
076900*                                                                *
077000*----------------------------------------------------------------*
077100
077200 RETURN-VALUE-OF-GOLDEN-RATIO.
077300     MOVE VALUE-GOLDEN-RATIO TO MATHPK-RESULT
077400     .

, so, I'm also posting it here. BTW, the stuff
comes from the ETKPAK library at http://www.etk.com
```

#### ↳ Re: Random Number Generator

- **From:** Albert Ratzlaff <albert@infonet.com.py>
- **Date:** 1998-07-09T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<35A4BA14.6CB9E912@infonet.com.py>`
- **References:** `<rdavis.63.001BF99D@ozemail.com.au>`

```
Ron Davis wrote:

> Hi all,
> I need a random number generator, (rough and ready will do, only for
…[10 more quoted lines elided]…
> Ron Davis

Here's an easy one that simulates the Unix 'random' call:

****************************************************
* cw-rnd    : Interfase para cp-rnd - numero random         (WS) *
****************************************************
      *
       01  CW-RND-AREAS.
           02  CW-RND-NUMERO           PIC 9(10).
           02  CW-RND-SGTE             PIC 9(9) COMP-4 VALUE 1.
           02  CW-RND-AUX              PIC 9(18).
      *

      ************************************************
* cp-rnd    : R.S. para obtener numero random (azar)        (PD) *
*           : Salida      :
CW-RND-NUMERO                                  *
****************************************************
*
       9999-OBTENER-NUMERO-RANDOM.
      *
           COMPUTE CW-RND-SGTE =
               (CW-RND-SGTE * 1103515245) + 12345.
           DIVIDE CW-RND-SGTE BY 65536 GIVING CW-RND-AUX.
           DIVIDE CW-RND-AUX BY 32768  GIVING CW-RND-AUX
                                       REMAINDER CW-RND-NUMERO.

      *

(Sorry about the formating and the language ;-)
It seems to work with RM/COBOL, allthough I have not done extensive
testing.

Regards
Albert Ratzlaff
```

#### ↳ Re: Who was DFH?

- **From:** Arnold Trembley <arnold.trembley@worldnet.att.net>
- **Date:** 1998-07-07T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<6nusv0$gm0@bgtnsc03.worldnet.att.net>`
- **References:** `<almacdEvr4uE.JJv@netcom.com>`

```
Al MacDonald wrote:
> 
> I am curious about the identity of "DFH", author of many of the
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
> PP-ASEL

I hope this is not bad netiquette, but I thought I would answer your
question by pasting in this posting from bit.listserv.cics-l that
appeared yesterday:

=====begin quote=====
Subject:	Re: CICS and its inventors
Date:		6 Jul 1998 17:48:41 GMT
From:		Bob Shair (courtesy) <rmshair@delphi.itg.uiuc.edu>
Organization:	University of Illinois at Urbana-Champaign
Newsgroups:	bit.listserv.vmesa-l, bit.listserv.cics-l
Followup-To:	bit.listserv.cics-l


Gregg Levine <hansolofalcon@worldnet.att.net> wrote:
> Hello from Gregg Levine:
> I am curious about something that is threading its way through this list
> earlier. Who really did invent the CICS bundle that is now available for
> nearly every platform including the ones talked about here?

Well that's WAY off-topic for vmesa-l; I suggest cics-l.

IIRC, CICS was originally developed at the IBM site in Des Plaines, IL
by Ben Riggins and Ray VanderFleet.  That would have been 1968.
Memory tells me that this was the "Insurance Industry" center, though
CICS was a co-development with NIPSCO, the Northern Indiana Public
Service Company in Hammond, IN.

Of the 8 initial modules, Ben wrote Task Control and Terminal Control,
and Ray wrote the others, File Control, Transient Data Control, 
Storage Control, Temporary Storage Control, Dump Control and
??? (I've lost one).

VM Connection: 

The development was done (under OS/MFT) on the SAME System 360/40
(serial number 2) on which CP-40 was originally developed at the
Cambridge Scientific Center.  Dynamic Address Translation was 
disabled, of course.
```

I thought CICS came out of Westi, which was created by Westinghouse then
stolen by IBM in a funky deal where IBM's contractors helped develop it for
Westinghouse and then had ownership rights to the software.  The first
'real' installation of Westi was at Amana Refrigeration (I guess it was an
appliance thing), which, lead IBM to develop CICS off that proto. 

	As for 'DFH' one of the guys that taught me VSAM eons ago, told me that it
was someones initials, which, I tend to believe.  For the life of me, I
can't remember the guy's that taught me VSAM's name, he helped develop VSAM
for IBM... all I can remember is that he was a drunk.  Which kind of
explains why vsam is such crap.

Andy

#### ↳ Re: Who was DFH?

On Wed, 8 Jul 1998 01:15:50, almacd@netcom.com (Al MacDonald) wrote:

> I am curious about the identity of "DFH", author of many of the 
> modules in CICS.  Anyone know who he was?
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> PP-ASEL

There are quite a few urban myths about DFH - but each of the following are WRONG:

Developed for Hursley
Dollars for Hursley
Denver Foot Hills
Denver Food Holding
Dumb, Fat, and Hapyy (<< I love this one)
(Initials of CICS author).  Ben Riggins did not have to change his name

It is just a unique IBM product code.  If memory serves me right, there actuaslly were some rules
to how this code was assigned many years ago.  The only rule left now is that initials A to I are reserved to
IBM, and other software vendors may register there own codes with IBM

Regards

Volker Bandke
(BSP GmbH)
```

## Thread: I'm confused! — 5 msgs

### I'm confused!

- **From:** "Codad" <codad@usa.net>
- **Date:** 1998-07-07T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<01bda956$88581f00$22b637d2@mark>`

```

I'm confused!  I keep hearing all the media reports and propaganda from
various recruitment agencies about how there is a worldwide shortage of
programmers to convert systems to be Y2K compliant.  So, being a COBOL
programmer, I thought I would see about getting a little contract work
converting exisiting systems across.

I have sent my details to dozens and dozens of IT recruitment/placement
companies as well as posting to relevant newsgroups.  So imagine my
amazement when I didn't receive a single offer of work.  The few responses
I did get were to simply inform me that they (whoever) had received my
details and that I had been added to a database for future reference.

I have been looking now for near on 6 months with still no response.  I am
gradually getting the impression that there is NO year 2000 problem and
that the whole issue is just plain media hype.

I have heard quoted that there are...
"3 million COBOL programmers required worldwide [to meet Y2K demand] but
only 40,000 available."
-- what a load of bull dust!!!

Mark Hallett
DHM Consulting
mark@timaru.com
```

<a id="t-6f286458d7"></a>
## Thread: Debugging Tools for Cobol for MVS and VM — 4 msgs

_Topics: [`Mainframe, z/OS, JCL, CICS`](topics.md#mainframe)_

### Debugging Tools for Cobol for MVS and VM

- **From:** David Abere <da2@columbia.edu>
- **Date:** 1998-07-07T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** bit.listserv.ibm-main,comp.lang.cobol,alt.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<Pine.GSO.3.95qL.980707164730.10656A-100000@sawasdee.cc.columbia.edu>`

```
We have found the DEBUG TOOL for COBOL for MVS and VM (rel 1.2) to be a
CPU and time hog at the present (for instance it took close to 5 CPU
minutes to run a simple display of 1 field from 45000 records as compared
to about 30 seconds CPU time in COBDBG(VS COBOL II).	

Does anyone know about any other similar debugging tools from vendors that
could help us here (yes our systems group has looked into it and they
cannot improve its performance).

One feature we would need is the ability to submit a job in MVS batch for
debugging purposes. Please feel free to email me at da2@columbia.edu
Thanks,
David
```

#### ↳ Re: Debugging Tools for Cobol for MVS and VM

- **From:** "Wayne L. Beavers" <wayneb@beyond-software.com>
- **Date:** 1998-07-07T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** bit.listserv.ibm-main,comp.lang.cobol,alt.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<35A299D0.3E64@beyond-software.com>`
- **References:** `<Pine.GSO.3.95qL.980707164730.10656A-100000@sawasdee.cc.columbia.edu>`

```
David Abere wrote:
> 
> We have found the DEBUG TOOL for COBOL for MVS and VM (rel 1.2) to be a
…[11 more quoted lines elided]…
> David

Have you looked at XPEDITER from Compuware?

About 5 years ago, me and another developer added the Batch Connect
Facility to XPEDITER. I don't work for Compuware any more. What it will
do is allow you to run the XPEDITER debugger under TSO/ISPF or TSO
without ISPF to debug a COBOL program running in a batch address space.
It requires a VTAM connection between the MVS batch system and the MVS
TSO system, unless of course it is a single machine.

A break point on a single statement should be pretty cheap. A breakpoint
is nothing more than a bad opcode inserted to cause a program check so
that the ESTAE routine can gain control to tell you that it happened.
Any verb without a breakpoint will run at full speed.

I have no idea if XPEDITER still supports the Batch Connect Facility.
You'll have to ask them. 
```

#### ↳ Re: Debugging Tools for Cobol for MVS and VM

- **From:** far@oes.fyns-amt.dk (Frank Allan Rasmussen)
- **Date:** 1998-07-08T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** bit.listserv.ibm-main,comp.lang.cobol,alt.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<35a312fb.487711@news.tele.dk>`
- **References:** `<Pine.GSO.3.95qL.980707164730.10656A-100000@sawasdee.cc.columbia.edu>`

```
On Tue, 7 Jul 1998 16:51:55 -0400, David Abere <da2@columbia.edu>
wrote:

>One feature we would need is the ability to submit a job in MVS batch for
>debugging purposes. Please feel free to email me at da2@columbia.edu

SmartTest from ViaSoft does this. I installed the product at an
installation I worked at a few years back. You can submit a batch job
and debug it from TSO/ISPF.

One thing with the ViaSoft products: You will need a password to
install, which can be anoying in the install process. Other than this
the product is fairly easy to install and use.

I think that Xpediter from Compuware has a simmilar feature, but I
only installed and used Xpediter/CICS so I can not say anything on the
batch usage.

But try to look at:
http://www.viasoft.com     or
http://www.compuware.com

	Frank Allan Rasmussen
	Systemprogrammer
    	Fyns Amts EDB-central
```

- **References:** `<1998061914422200.KAA06521@ladder03.news.aol.com>`

```

I've used Microfocus Cobol to create cgi-bin programs for Apache / HP-UX.
That's just plain Microfocus - you don't have to buy any special add-ins to do
this.

I used Cobol because:
(1) We already had it bought, installed and tested.
(2) It included Oracle support (embedded SQL)
(3) We have LOTS of Cobol programmers in-house.

If you're interested, e-mail me and I'll send you some sample source.
It's actually pretty easy to do.

<a id="t-bedcd21376"></a>
## Thread: Help With Cobol Syntax — 6 msgs

_Topics: [`Help requests and how-to`](topics.md#help)_

### Help With Cobol Syntax

- **From:** limlc@purdue.edu (Lim)
- **Date:** 1998-07-08T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<35a37769.5097377@news.purdue.edu>`

```
Hi,
Need some advice.. What's the easiest way to check each and every
character and make sure it's alphbet.  The word is stored in a PIC X.
How can I go from character to character?
Thanks
L.C. Lim
```

#### ↳ Re: Help With Cobol Syntax

- **From:** "Leif Svalgaard" <leif@ibm.net>
- **Date:** 1998-07-08T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<35a37a3f.0@news1.ibm.net>`
- **References:** `<35a37769.5097377@news.purdue.edu>`

```

Lim wrote in message <35a37769.5097377@news.purdue.edu>...
>Need some advice.. What's the easiest way to check each and every
>character and make sure it's alphbet.  The word is stored in a PIC X.
>How can I go from character to character?


01  test-me-ok                   pic x(20)   value "is alphabetic".
01  test-me-not-ok            pic x(20)   value "a'int alphabetic".

if test-me-ok is  alphabetic
     perform xxxx
.
if test-me-not-ok is not alphabetic
     perform zzzz
```

#### ↳ Re: Help With Cobol Syntax

- **From:** scomstock@aol.com (S Comstock)
- **Date:** 1998-07-08T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1998070813574900.JAA06390@ladder03.news.aol.com>`
- **References:** `<35a37769.5097377@news.purdue.edu>`

```
L.C.Lim writes ...

>Hi,
>Need some advice.. What's the easiest way to check each and every
>character and make sure it's alphbet.  The word is stored in a PIC X.
>How can I go from character to character?
>Thanks

Sounds like homework to me. We don't generally do homework for people. But
here's a hint: alphabetic, alphabetic-lower, alphabetic-upper.

Cheers,


Steve Comstock
Telephone: 303-393-8716
www.trainersfriend.com
email: steve@trainersfriend.com
256-B S. Monaco Parkway
Denver, CO 80224
USA
```

Lim,

    The ALPHABETIC test will be true if the field contains any Alphabetic

    Subsequently, I believe you could test the field for ALPHABETIC and NOT
EQUAL TO SPACE to ensure Alphabetic only.

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Job name

- **From:** "AM" <AM69107@glaxowellcome.com>
- **Date:** 1998-07-08T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<01bdaa88$def58b30$c58c3398@us0071826>`
- **References:** `<6nvsse$s1k@info.telenor.no> <6o01i9$qn2$1@juliana.sprynet.com>`

```
this came from another thread...  it helped me... hope it does the same for
you...


       Identification Division.
         Program-ID. Cob2Job.
         Author. Gilbert Saint-flour <gsf@ibm.net>.
       Data Division.
        Working-Storage Section.
         01 job-name Pic x(8).
         01 proc-step Pic x(8).
         01 step-name Pic x(8).
         01 job-number Pic x(8).
         01 program-name Pic x(8).
         01 user-id Pic x(8).
         01 group-name Pic x(8).
         01 user-name Pic x(20).
         01 four-bytes. 05 full-word Pic s9(8) Comp.
        Linkage Section.
         01 cb1.  05 ptr1 Pointer Occurs 256.
         01 cb2.  05 ptr2 Pointer Occurs 256.
       Procedure Division.
 PSA       SET Address Of cb1 To NULL.
 TCB       SET Address Of cb1 To ptr1(136)
 TIOT      SET Address Of cb2 To ptr1(4)
           MOVE cb2(1:8) To job-name
           MOVE cb2(9:8) To proc-step
           MOVE cb2(17:8) To step-name
 JSCB      SET Address Of cb2 To ptr1(46)
           MOVE cb2(361:8) To program-name
 SSIB      SET Address Of cb2 To ptr2(80)
           MOVE cb2(13:8) To job-number
 PSA       SET Address Of cb1 To NULL.
 ASCB      SET Address Of cb1 To ptr1(138)
 ASXB      SET Address Of cb2 To ptr1(28)
           MOVE cb2(193:8) To user-id
 ACEE      SET Address Of cb2 To ptr2(51)
           MOVE cb2(31:8) To group-name
 UNAM      SET Address Of cb1 To ptr2(26)
           MOVE zero to full-word.
           MOVE cb1(1:1) To four-bytes(4:1)
           MOVE cb1(2:full-word) To user-name
           DISPLAY job-name ' '
                   proc-step ' '
                   step-name ' '
                   job-number ' '
                   program-name ' '
                   user-id ' '
                   group-name  ' '
                   user-name  ' '
           GOBACK.


WOB <wobconsult@sprynet.com> wrote in article

#### ↳ Re: Job name

- **From:** zberger@ldl.net
- **Date:** 1998-07-10T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<6o5hgr$k7l$1@nnrp1.dejanews.com>`
- **References:** `<6nvsse$s1k@info.telenor.no>`

```
In article <6nvsse$s1k@info.telenor.no>,
  "Svein Gr�e" <svein.grae@fou.telenor.no> wrote:
> Hi,
>
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
> this one is easy:

working-storage section.
01 cvt.
 02 cvt-addr pic s9(8) comp value +16.
 02 cvt-ptr  pointer redefines cvt-addr.

linkage section.
01 ptrs.
 02 ptr-area.
  03 ptr-0  pointer.
  03 ptr-4  pointer.
  03 ptr-8  pointer.
  03 ptr-12 pointer.
 02 dat-area redefines ptr-area.
  03 jobname  pic x(8).
  03 procname pic x(8).
  03 stepname pic x(8).

procedure division.

* address communications vector table
  set address of ptrs to cvt-ptr

* address task control block list
  set address of ptrs to ptr-0

* address current tcb
  set address of ptrs to ptr-0

* address tiot
  set address of ptrs to ptr-0

  display 'jobname  : ' jobname
  display 'procname : ' procname
  display 'stepname : ' stepname
  goback

-----== Posted via Deja News, The Leader in Internet Discussion ==-----
http://www.dejanews.com/rg_mkgrp.xp   Create Your Own Free Member Forum
```

## Thread: history of cobol — 1 this month / 10 total

_Topics: [`COBOL's future, legacy, and obsolescence`](topics.md#future)_

_Thread started [1998-06](1998-06.md#t-908a4b4e0c)._

##### ↳ ↳ Re: history of cobol

- **From:** "Dave Checkley" <dcheckl@ibm.net>
- **Date:** 1998-07-08T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<vggagiccaantyy.pminews@myhostname>`
- **References:** `<358DD9B7.74B5@infoave.net> <6mm1ht$klj$1@nnrp1.dejanews.com> <Sqxj1.66$ei3.213015@news4.atl.bellsouth.net> <6momh8$uqk$1@nnrp1.dejanews.com> <_xWj1.438$ei3.1088523@news4.atl.bellsouth.net>`

```
On Tue, 23 Jun 1998 23:06:34 GMT, Judson McClendon wrote:

:>Actually, whether you realize it or not, I was paying you a compliment.
:>Either your message was a clever troll (meaning you didn't really believe
:>what you were saying, you were just posting it to get a rise out of us),
:>or you are abysmally ignorant of the facts.  Not thinking anyone could be
:>quite so ignorant of the facts, I assumed your message was a clever troll.
:>Now you disillusion me by saying you really are that ignorant of the
:>facts, and not really clever enough to have written that message as a
:>troll.  I hereby publicly apoligize, and retract my compliment.  Does that
:>make you feel better?
:>
:>Now, since I must retract my compliment of your post as a clever troll,
:>I will comment on a few of your serious misconceptions.  I have copied
:>your original post below for comment.
:>

followed by some very good comments. 

Judson, I am in total agreement with you. COBOL was developed for commercial
data processing, in the days when computers, and their ancilliary resources
(dasd, programmers, etc) were difficult to acquire.

COBOL is still the language of choice for commercial data processing - I am
working on a project implementing credit/debit card processing for over 5
million cards (with normal growth, we'll probably have over 10 million in the
portfolio in 5 year's time, and who knows where we'll be in 15 years time -
maybe 100 million?). The language is, of course, COBOL in the backend, where
the real work gets done. We can afford to use OO languages on the front-end
PCs, which can afford dedicated processors for each user, but when we get
around to large integrated centralized databases, we need efficient,
reliable, maintable and stable software suites.

As an aside, Ihave seen many complaints about C/C++ memory management - there
seems to be a fundamental flaw in the language design which COBOL does not
suffer from.

Dave Checkley
```

<a id="t-3d7e49e67b"></a>
## Thread: FD vs W/S — 1 msgs

_Topics: [`VSAM, files, sorting`](topics.md#files)_

### Re: FD vs W/S

- **From:** "Leif Svalgaard" <leif@ibm.net>
- **Date:** 1998-07-08T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<35a41090.0@news1.ibm.net>`
- **References:** `<6nuibt$cs6$1@birch.prod.itd.earthlink.net> <1998070804295400.AAA29756@ladder01.news.aol.com> <6o0sbe$f75$1@news.ses.cio.eds.com>`

```
>This issue has been discussed in this forum in recent months, and I have
>some questions...
>Since there are 25+ segments, that is alot of stuff in working storage.
>
>Here's how I did it.  I defined my FD statement to have multiple 01
levels -
>a generic 15 byte area to decide how to process each segment, and then
areas
>for each segment type.  The way I understand it, these 01s redefine the
same
>area, which is only as big as the largest segment type.
>
>I think that this would make a big difference in efficiency, size, etc of
>the program.  Am I over-estimating this?  Are the considerations regarding
>stability of content in the buffer more important?


You could have redefined the 01 levels in working storage as well with
almost
the same amount of saving and without the danger of undefined data in the
FD.
```

<a id="t-85a892b514"></a>
## Thread: What's CSP? — 1 this month / 2 total

_Thread started [1998-06](1998-06.md#t-85a892b514)._

#### ↳ Re: What's CSP?

- **From:** "AEDComS" <AEDComS@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 1998-07-08T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<BZBo1.1680$Xe6.1174914@news2.randori.com>`
- **References:** `<1998062014202000.KAA06411@ladder03.news.aol.com> <35923c90.22172387@10.100.250.58>`

```
well depends on what version you are talking about... most CSP shops use
V3.3. This version does not yet generate the code into COBOL nor C.  no GUI
interface either. Just plain CICS like mainframe textbased screens. sure you
can do pop-ups... but you have to code for it!!!! and define maps....
floating points...etc...

CSP, on my opinion, is just one of the attempts to simplify COBOL/CICS
programming, NOT!!  as one of my co-workers say, it is just one way of
complicating COBOL.

CSP has about 12 verbs to use in programming. so it is very very easy to
learn.

V4 i think is the version that would do COBOL generation. The visual Gen /
visual Age
products is the new offering of IBM that will do internet commerce.

a good COBOL programmer can do CSP in no time.  but be ready to re-think how
you
do your "structured programming"...

## Thread: Job Opportunity - Mainframe COBOL training program - Starts again on July 2th in Troy, MI — 1 msgs

_Topics: [`Jobs, careers, recruiting, salary`](topics.md#jobs) · [`Mainframe, z/OS, JCL, CICS`](topics.md#mainframe)_

### Job Opportunity - Mainframe COBOL training program - Starts again on July 2th in Troy, MI

- **From:** "Richard Ickes" <rwi@ic.net>
- **Date:** 1998-07-08T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<35a2fad8.0@news.ic.net>`

```
Job Opportunity

COMPANY:  SYNTEL Inc.              
ADDRESS:  2800 Livernois Road Suite 400
          Troy, MI 48083
TYPE OF COMPANY : Software Consulting 
INTERNET SITE: SYNTELINC.COM

CONTACT PERSON : Joseph Rahal
PHONE : (248) 619-3598
FAX   : (248) 619-2890
E-MAIL: Joseph_Rahal@syntelinc.com

JOB TITLE : Associate Programmer - Entry Level   (F/T)

JOB DESC  :  Program consists of 8-weeks of training of instructional course
work and focuses on, but is not limited to, COBOL, DB2, IMS and CICS,
followed by a 3 to 6 month mentoring program.  Upon completion of the
programs, the individual will be promoted to programmer and placed on a
SYNTEL client project.

APPLICANTS : Interested applicants should have a 2 year degree in Computer
Science or a 4 year degree in any discipline computer-related or
non-computer related or have prior business experience with a strong
aptitude for programming. 

WAGES : $26K - $32K/yr (Yes, you are paid during the training process)  
Benefits : Yes

REMARKS : All candidates MUST be willing to relocate.  Applicants who wish
to be considered can fax, mail or e-mail their resume.  All candidates must
be U.S. Citizen or Permanent Resident.
```

<a id="t-2bb68c6a75"></a>
## Thread: Question — 20 msgs

### Question

- **From:** "Warren G. Simmons" <warrens@iname.com>
- **Date:** 1998-07-09T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<35A4F7CF.AE7E962D@iname.com>`

```
For COBOL:

Are there functions or features that you see as vendor dependant that
you feel could/should be standardized?

Serious comments would aid my efforts to catch up with the status of of
the current and proposed standard.

Sharing the results of your responses (should there be any) will be
insured if you post to the group. However, private comments are also
encouraged.

Thank you for reading and considering a response.

Warren Simmons
```

#### ↳ Re: Question

- **From:** redsky@ibm.net (Thane Hubbell)
- **Date:** 1998-07-10T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<Jl0PnHJ5PvPd-pn2-4ZdgGMwWWMvQ@Dwight_Miller.iix.com>`
- **References:** `<35A4F7CF.AE7E962D@iname.com>`

```
On Thu, 9 Jul 1998 17:03:11, "Warren G. Simmons" <warrens@iname.com> 
wrote:

> For COBOL:
> 
…[11 more quoted lines elided]…
> 


Warren,

I'd like to see an "On Exception" phrase added to the intrinsic 
functions.  When you make a call to the date functions, or to the 
numval function, if there is invalid data in the field, it usually 
blows up and abends the job.  (On any of 3 compilers I tried!).

On exception would let us trap these errors and would be very handy.  
Thanks.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Question

- **From:** "Wayne L. Beavers" <wayneb@beyond-software.com>
- **Date:** 1998-07-10T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<35A67DF8.5EE3@beyond-software.com>`
- **References:** `<35A4F7CF.AE7E962D@iname.com> <Jl0PnHJ5PvPd-pn2-4ZdgGMwWWMvQ@Dwight_Miller.iix.com>`

```
Thane Hubbell wrote:
> 
> 
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
> Thanks.

You should be able to trap any condition. PL/I will allow that. How
about:

On condition(B37) (or E37, etc.)
On condition(222) (Well, even PL/I won't allow that)
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Question

- **From:** Bob Berman <bberman@netbox.com>
- **Date:** 1998-07-10T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<35A6BF00.57D4@netbox.com>`

Thane Hubbell wrote:
 
> I'd like to see an "On Exception" phrase added to the intrinsic
> functions.  When you make a call to the date functions, or to the
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
> Thanks.

I'd like to be able to trap all error conditions in Cobol, as can be
done in PL/I.  It certainly cuts down on late night production support
calls if the offending transaction can be thrown out without stopping
the processing cycle, and then researched in the morning.

Bob
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Question

```

Thane Hubbell wrote in message ...
[...]
>Warren,
>
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
>
Thane,

You mentioned the date and numval functions. In the new standard
we will have TEST-DATE-... and TEST-NUMVAL-... which appears to
provide a means to prevent the stated problems.

Furthermore, it appears that invalid data in an argument to an
intrinsic function would trigger the EC-ARGUMENT-FUNCTION
exception condition; which could be processed by the program.
---------------------
Rick Smith
e-mail: < ricksmith@aiservices.com >
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Question

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** "Rick Smith" <ricksmith@aiservices.com>
- **Date:** 1998-07-13T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<cXeq1.71$p4.244567@news1.atlantic.net>`
- **References:** `<35A4F7CF.AE7E962D@iname.com> <Jl0PnHJ5PvPd-pn2-4ZdgGMwWWMvQ@Dwight_Miller.iix.com> <Gywp1.41$CH.260124@news1.atlantic.net> <01bdadf6$c7f93500$47bc48a6@default>`

```

Thane Hubbell wrote in message <01bdadf6$c7f93500$47bc48a6@default>...
>
>
…[32 more quoted lines elided]…
>
First, a warning! Not having seen any examples or other information
about the new exception options, I have to translate from the standard,
part of which is implementor defined. This means that what I am
presenting is my interpretation of the meaning of the "proposed"
standard. I am using CD 1.2. Having said that, here goes!

For the TEST-DATE-... example.

01 BAD-DATE PIC 9(8) VALUE 19991301. *> Bad Month
01 GOOD-DATE-INTEGER PIC 9(8) VALUE 0.
01 DATE-ERROR PIC X(23).
...
>> CONSTANT SIMPLE-DATE-TEST IS 0
MOVE SPACES TO DATE-ERROR
MOVE ZERO TO GOOD-DATE-INTEGER
>> IF SIMPLE-DATE-TEST = 1
IF FUNCTION TEST-DATE-YYYYMMDD (BAD-DATE) NOT = 0
    MOVE "INVALID DATE" TO DATE-ERROR
ELSE
    MOVE "NO ERROR" TO DATE-ERROR
    MOVE FUNCTION DATE-OF-INTEGER (BAD-DATE)
        TO GOOD-DATE-INTEGER
END-IF
>> ELSE
EVALUATE FUNCTION TEST-DATE-YYYYMMDD (BAD-DATE)
  WHEN 3
    MOVE "INVALID DAY" TO DATE-ERROR
  WHEN 2
    MOVE "INVALID MONTH"
        TO DATE-ERROR *> Executed for this example
WHEN 1
    MOVE "INVALID YEAR" TO DATE-ERROR
  WHEN 0
    MOVE "NO ERROR" TO DATE-ERROR
    MOVE FUNCTION DATE-OF-INTEGER (BAD-DATE)
        TO GOOD-DATE-INTEGER
  WHEN OTHER
    MOVE "INVALID FUNCTION RETURN"
        TO DATE-ERROR *> Broken compiler
END-EVALUATE
>> END-IF
...

For the EC-ARGUMENT-FUNCTION example:

01 BAD-DATE PIC 9(8) VALUE 19991301. *> Bad Month
01 GOOD-DATE-INTEGER PIC 9(8) VALUE 0.
01 DATE-IN-ERROR BINARY-CHAR VALUE 0.
...
USE AFTER EXCEPTION EC-ARGUMENT-FUNCTION.
  *> USE procedure is processed for any function
  *> if the exception has been activated by a
  *> TURN preprocessor directive
  *> in this case, we are only concerned about the date
    MOVE 1 TO DATE-IN-ERROR
    RESUME
    .
...
MOVE ZERO TO GOOD-DATE-INTEGER
MOVE ZERO TO DATE-IN-ERROR
>> TURN EC-ARGUMENT-FUNCTION CHECKING ON
MOVE FUNCTION DATE-OF-INTEGER (BAD-DATE)
        TO GOOD-DATE-INTEGER
>> TURN EC-ARGUMENT-FUNCTION CHECKING OFF
IF DATE-IN-ERROR NOT = 0
    *> perform bad date processing
END-IF
...

Certainly, for date and number processing, the TEST-DATE
and TEST-NUMVAL functions are preferred. For other
conditions, there are numerous EC-... for which USE procedures
may be written.
------------------------
Rick Smith
e-mail: < ricksmith@aiservices.com >
```

them.

Warren,

There was just a post where Claus H. wanted to do this:
EVALUATE WSWA-PRIORITY
  WHEN 'HIGH'
   OR  'H'
     ...
  WHEN 'MEDIUM'
   OR  'M'
     ...
  WHEN 'LOW'
   OR  'L'
    ...
END-EVALUATE

and got in trouble. I know that you can do it like this:
EVALUATE WSWA-PRIORITY
  WHEN 'HIGH'  some thing
  WHEN 'H' same thing
     ...
  WHEN 'MEDIUM' some thing
  WHEN 'M' same thing
    ...
END-EVALUATE

But this solution means duplication of code (some -> same).
What Claus wants is actually quite natural and useful.
```

Leif Svalgaard wrote:
> 
> There was just a post where Claus H. wanted to do this:
…[23 more quoted lines elided]…
> What Claus wants is actually quite natural and useful.

Actually, you can do this...

  EVALUATE WSWA-PRIORITY
    WHEN 'HIGH'
    WHEN 'H'
      [...SOMETHING...]
    WHEN 'MEDIUM'
    WHEN 'M'
      [...SOMETHING ELSE...]
    ...
  END-EVALUATE

It took me a long time to realize this.  Why it isn't something more logical like
   WHEN 'HIGH' OR 'H'
   or
   WHEN 'HIGH' 'H'
...I have no idea...
```
