- **References:** `<6o9u98$ifh@bgtnsc02.worldnet.att.net>`

```
In article <6o9u98$ifh@bgtnsc02.worldnet.att.net>, Bill Lynch <wblynch@att.net>
writes:

>I don't know C; but isn't what you've described the essence of a case
>structure, i.e., where you fall thru one case after another until you
>either get a hit or you fall out the end?

In C, in a switch statement, one can have multiple case statements labeling
statements to be executed. However, unlike COBOL, when a matching case
statement value is encountered, all statements after that point are executed
(even statements for subsequent case statements) until either the end of the
switch construct is encountered or a break statement is encountered.

In COBOL, in an EVALUATE statement, one can have multiple WHEN statements
labeling a set of imperative statements, but (unlike C) when the last
imperative statement associated with a WHEN (or a series of consecutive WHENs)
is executed, control goes to the end of the EVALUATE statement, maing a "break"
statement unnecessary, but also making it impossible to drop through to the
next set of imperative statements. (Actually, I prefer COBOL's way because the
C way can easily lead to more statements being executed than one had
intended--just by forgetting to code a "break" statement. Also, COBOL is more
flexable in what is allowed in the EVALUATE expression and WHEN expressions.)

Mark A. Young
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Question

_(thread depth: 6)_

- **From:** Bill Lynch <wblynch@att.net>
- **Date:** 1998-07-12T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<6obuol$238@bgtnsc03.worldnet.att.net>`
- **References:** `<6o9u98$ifh@bgtnsc02.worldnet.att.net> <1998071217422700.NAA19251@ladder01.news.aol.com>`

```

> 
> In article <6o9u98$ifh@bgtnsc02.worldnet.att.net>, Bill Lynch <wblynch@att.net>
…[21 more quoted lines elided]…
>

structure (not in my experience, at least). 'Never heard of one before
which didn't stop when it hit a match.

Bill Lynch

> Mark A. Young
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Question

- **From:** mark0young@aol.com (Mark0Young)
- **Date:** 1998-07-11T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1998071103173200.XAA13794@ladder03.news.aol.com>`
- **References:** `<35a67cc0.0@news1.ibm.net>`

```
In article <35a67cc0.0@news1.ibm.net>, "Leif Svalgaard" <leif@ibm.net> writes:

>There was just a post where Claus H. wanted to do this:
>EVALUATE WSWA-PRIORITY
…[22 more quoted lines elided]…
>What Claus wants is actually quite natural and useful.

You can have multiple WHEN clauses to perform the same imperative statements,
e.g.,

 EVALUATE WSWA-PRIORITY
    WHEN 'HIGH'
    WHEN 'H'
        some code (will be executed for both HIGH and H
    WHEN 'MEDIUM'
    WHEN 'M'
        some other code (will be executed for both MEDIUM and M)
    WHEN OTHER
         code for when none of the above WHENs match WSWA-PRIORITY
 END-EVALUATE

If you want a "throw-away WHEN", the imperative statement CONTINUE can be used,
e.g.,

 EVALUATE WSWA-PRIORITY
   WHEN 'HIGH'
   WHEN 'H'
   WHEN 'MEDIUM'
   WHEN 'M'
   WHEN 'LOW'
   WHEN 'L'
      CONTINUE
   WHEN OTHER
       PERFORM PRIORITY-ERROR-ROUTINE
 END-EVALUATE

Mark A. Young
```

## Thread: HELP : how to read packed comp-3 fields in my pc ??? — 3 msgs

_Topics: [`Language features and syntax`](topics.md#syntax) · [`Help requests and how-to`](topics.md#help)_

### HELP : how to read packed comp-3 fields in my pc ???

- **From:** "News Server" <rimon@hotmail.com>
- **Date:** 1998-07-09T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<6o2pvh$j42$1@lnews.actcom.co.il>`

```
Hi,
Im doing some data warehouse project that includes lots of data migration
from
IBM MF to NT, Im getting Flat files from the MF and they are in EBCDIC and
comp-3.
I know the structure if the records, and I know how to translate the EBCDIC,
my only problem is how to read the comp-3 fields.
if any one can please tell me how the format works...


thank you.

Rimon.

Applicom Software Ltd.

rimon@applicom.co.il
```

#### ↳ Re: HELP : how to read packed comp-3 fields in my pc ???

- **From:** "Dave Johnson" <systemad@globalnet.co.uk>
- **Date:** 1998-07-09T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<6o391t$hba$4@heliodor.xara.net>`
- **References:** `<6o2pvh$j42$1@lnews.actcom.co.il>`

```
News Server wrote in message <6o2pvh$j42$1@lnews.actcom.co.il>...
>Hi,
>Im doing some data warehouse project that includes lots of data migration
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>I know the structure if the records, and I know how to translate the
EBCDIC,
>my only problem is how to read the comp-3 fields.
>if any one can please tell me how the format works...
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
>


IBM Mainframe COMP-3 also known as packed data (PD) because,
amazingly, the data is (or are) packed! Works like this........

Each digit occupies 1/2 byte (4 bits) and the last 4 bits are used for the
sign. A PD field can only be a full number of bytes, so if you specify an
even number of digits, the compiler assumes a leading zero.

The IBM normally uses 'C' for a positive sign, 'D' for a negative (there
are some packages which use 'F' for positive, but this is treated as a
'C' for arithmetic compares. If you don't declare the field as signed, I
believe a 'C' is assumed (I would stand correction on that, may be 'F').

Examples:

Assuming a field defined as PIC S9(7) COMP-3   (4 bytes)......

+123456   would be held as  x'0123456C'
-123456    would be held as  x'0123456D'

For a larger field PIC S9(11) COMP-3  (6 bytes)

+123456  would be held as  x'00000123456C'
-123456  would be held as   x'00000123456D'

(hope I counted them correctly).

One thing to note - a PD field does not hold the decimal place - this
is defined as a 'V' in the picture (eg PIC S9(5)V99 which will hold 7
digits, and will perform the alignment on arithmetic operations and
decimal moves). So if the first example was S9(5)V99 instead of
S9(7), the actual value would be +/- 1234.56.

Hope that helps,
DaveJ.
```

#### ↳ Re: HELP : how to read packed comp-3 fields in my pc ???

- **From:** Ken Foskey <waratah@zip.com.au>
- **Date:** 1998-07-13T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<35A8DC4E.CE7B4C5@zip.com.au>`
- **References:** `<6o2pvh$j42$1@lnews.actcom.co.il>`

```
Rimon,

I know that you said that you know how to convert from EBCDIC but just
in case:  If you translate using FTP or whatever the COMP-3 fields will
be lost forever.  The translation from EBCDIC to ASCII will make the
data very unreadable.

I hope that you are doing a binary transfer and reading it internally in
your conversion program, in this case Dave's infomation will work for
you.n

Good luck
Ken


News Server wrote:
> 
> Hi,
…[14 more quoted lines elided]…
> rimon@applicom.co.il
```

## Thread: Random Number Generator — 5 msgs

Intrinsic functions were made an _optional_ part of the standard. That means a
compiler could include them or omit them, and in both cases be able to call
itself compliant with the '85 standard (assuming it met the other criteria).

Mark A. Young

## Thread: Cobol run time library not installed — 6 msgs

### Cobol run time library not installed

- **From:** "Renaat Casteels" <lmfocus@skynet.be>
- **Date:** 1998-07-09T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<6o2ps7$ltj$1@news0.skynet.be>`

```
I wan't to run MF Cobol in a dos box on Nt 4.0.
I get the message cobol run time library not installed

Could anybody please help me !!!
With friendly regards
Renaat Casteels
```

#### ↳ Re: Cobol run time library not installed

- **From:** "Leif Svalgaard" <leif@ibm.net>
- **Date:** 1998-07-09T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<35a4f05f.0@news1.ibm.net>`
- **References:** `<6o2ps7$ltj$1@news0.skynet.be>`

```

Renaat Casteels wrote in message <6o2ps7$ltj$1@news0.skynet.be>...
>I wan't to run MF Cobol in a dos box on Nt 4.0.
>I get the message cobol run time library not installed

Depending on what versions and other things, this could easy or hard.
Here are some things that I do:


You need to do something like this (in autoexec for the box)
where you change MF to point to where the compiler

@echo off
REM  The following lines should be placed in a DOS CONFIG.SYS
REM  FILES=100
REM  BUFFERS=10
REM
REM  The following lines should be placed in AUTOEXEC.BAT
SET MF=%ETKDIR%\MF
PATH=%MF%\BIN;%PATH%
SET COBDIR=%MF%\BIN
SET LIB=%MF%\LIB
SET INCLUDE=%MF%\SOURCE;
SET HELPFILES=%MF%\HELP;
SET INIT=%MF%\INIT;


MF does some nasty stuff trying to prevent you from using dos compilers
under Windows. If you get a complaint that a certain windows module is
not found, make a bat file (e.g. mycob.bat) like this:

@echo off
echo Compiling %1...
debug %cobdir%\cob.exe %1.cob,%1.obj,nul,nul
use"%etkdir%\d.dir"<%etkdir%\q>nul
if errorlevel 1  goto compile_error
goto end

:compile_error
debug %cobdir%\cob.exe %1.cob,%1.obj,nul,nul use"%etkdir%d.dir"<%etkdir%\q
echo error > %1.err
if exist %1.int del %1.int > nul
:end



----------------
where the little file q must contain:
g
q


This works because the dos debug program pretends that windows is not
present.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Cobol run time library not installed

- **From:** "Gael Wilson" <gw@mfltd.co.uk>
- **Date:** 1998-07-10T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<01bdabd6$f3c70760$905481c1@gw-nt>`
- **References:** `<6o2ps7$ltj$1@news0.skynet.be> <35a4f05f.0@news1.ibm.net> <35a4f1ab.0@news1.ibm.net>`

```
Leif,

I assume that you are using a 16-bit version of Micro Focus COBOL eg 3.2 or
3.4. Correct ? If so, the problem is likely to be because the EXEs are
dual-mode DOS-OS/2 executables and NT will attempt to run the OS/2 part.
So, to get it to work you need to add the directory containing your
executables eg \cobol\exedll to the Os2LibPath environment variable. Once
you have done that it should work. Alternatively you could use FORCEDOS to
run the DOS part of the executable.

I hope this helps.


Leif Svalgaard <leif@ibm.net> wrote in article
<35a4f1ab.0@news1.ibm.net>...
> Leif Svalgaard wrote in message <35a4f05f.0@news1.ibm.net>...

#### ↳ Re: Cobol run time library not installed

- **From:** riplin@kcbbs.gen.nz (Richard Plinston)
- **Date:** 1998-07-10T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3298190.75903.15574@kcbbs.gen.nz>`
- **References:** `<6o2ps7$ltj$1@news0.skynet.be>`

```
In message <<6o2ps7$ltj$1@news0.skynet.be>> "Renaat Casteels" <lmfocus@skynet.be> writes:
[MF Cobol in NT DOS box]
> I get the message cobol run time library not installed
> 

MF Cobol 2.x and 3.x supports DOS, Win3.x and OS/2 1.x 16bit.
When run in an NT DOS box it detects availability of protected
mode and tries to start up as if it were OS/2.  This then
fails when the run time goes belly up.

Try using FORCEDOS to run it.
```

> >/SERIOUS on

8<

> >/JOKE on

8<

> >/JOKE off (to get SERIOUS default)

8<

> Froggy:
>
> I always thought you had to have a terminating /SERIOUS off command.
> Are you telling me that a /JOKE off command automatically sets
> /SERIOUS on?

/JOKE offBob,

Both /serious and /joke work on the same serious bit: 0 = fun, 1 = not
rem /SERIOUS on sets 1
rem /SERIOUS off sets 0
rem /JOKE on sets 0
rem /JOKE off sets 1
The rems are to keep it on!

The Frog
```

<a id="t-5979a42ba6"></a>
## Thread: The Demise of COBOL Part II — 10 msgs

### The Demise of COBOL Part II

- **From:** john@ccpl.carr.lib.md.us
- **Date:** 1998-07-10T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<6o667t$mub$1@nnrp1.dejanews.com>`

```
Now, what is wrong with the alphabet soup of standard bodies (j4, g4, 9x
etc.) appropriating the zippiest features of all existing languages and
adding them to COBOL? Well, we already have a cautionary example in fairly
recent history. IBM and a few others thought it would be great to combine the
best features of COBOL, FORTRAN, Algol and even assembler to create the Swiss
Army knife of programming languages. They called it PL/I and it was launched
with all the power of IBM's marketing machine. This was back in thedthe days
of real account control by IBM. They said defecate, and the adoring customers
asked how high and what color.But despite the formidable power of IBM's
marketing machine behind it PL/I laid an egg with commercial accounts. It was
too big, had too many features, required too much machine resource. People
with COBOL type problems stuck with COBOL and folks with FORTRAN type
problems stuck with FORTRAN.

The new COBOL will face the same problem. The enthusiasts who want to cram in
every available feature from all these other languages will in fact use the
other languages in preference to COBOL when the situation calls for their use.
Lets face it, it is easier to write C++ in C++ than it is in any possible
version of of COBOL.


What exactly IS the COBOL market? It is defined by three factors, legacy
programs, legacy programmers and the failure of more modern languages to
address directly the commercial programming problem. The new features won't
assist legacy programs. They won't convert legacy programmers to object
oriented methods (can't teach us old dogs new tricks - as many firms have
discovered.) And they won't address better the problems that COBOL already
addresses very well accounts receivable etc. The 9x standard will be the one
that finally puts COBOL under. All the manufacturers will feel the need to
keep up with the standard, and the resulting compilers (and their manuals!)
will cause mass confusion in programming shops around the world. We already
have a generational split, where new graduates are surprised to find their
employers ignoring large chunks of COBOL 85. With COBOL 9x we will have the
tower of Babel. New programmers will be writing code (per their CS professor)
that older programmers	can't begin to decipher. And the language will
finally die.

John Culleton, CDP
Ancient COBOL Crank


The ne

Your opinions regarding PL/1 seem to be correct.  When I was attending
Purdue U. in the mid 70's I had to take a Data Structures class where
the pre-req was either Cobol or PL/1 since the majority of class
assignments were allegedly to be programmed in those languages.  Upon
actually taking the course all 30 students in the class were astounded
to find out that *all* of the class assignments were to be coded in
PL/1.  None of us had ever taken PL/1.  All had taken either Cobol or
Assembler or RPG or all 3.  Only 1 person got a grade above D in the
class (and it wasn't me).

Later on, while doing some work for a client bank in Nicosia, Cyprus I
came across an ATM system that was 90% PL/1.  I don't remember the
name of the package, but it was authored in China.  I had also heard
that PL/1 was, at one time, very popular in Europe.  Did IBM market it
more aggressively there than in the U.S.?

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: The Demise of COBOL Part II

- **From:** theodp@aol.com (Theo DP)
- **Date:** 1998-07-15T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1998071503214300.XAA01918@ladder03.news.aol.com>`
- **References:** `<35ab702b.2108900@news.apk.net>`

```
><HTML><PRE>Subject: Re: The Demise of COBOL Part II
>From: stevewie@apk.dot.net (SkippyPB)
…[89 more quoted lines elided]…
></PRE></HTML>

Having made my living using both, I can honestly say that I MUCH prefer PL/I to
COBOL and it's a vastly superior language. 
 
Why then did it fail to catch hold? 

IMHO: 

1. They charged too much - monthly maintenance was about ten times more than
COBOL. This is an error that continues to this day on the Windows platform -
Visual Age For Java is about $29 after rebate and runs on WIN 95; Visual Age
For PL/I is $2000+ and only runs on NT.

2. They forgot the business programmer - SEARCH or SORT verbs, the bread and
butter of business programming, were omitted in favor of such obtuse constructs
as 'CALL PLISRTx'.  

3. It was a little slow - optimized PL/I ran about twice as slow as optimized
COBOL due to such features as dynamically allocated variables. This counted
back in the old days (as many a dismayed Y2K worker can attest to!). 

4. Lack of education/books/PR/salesmanship - you'd never know that essentially
everything you could do with COBOL could be done with PL/I, and usually much
easier (e.g., inline DOs, 'real' initialization of variables, variable length
records/strings, string handling). In addition, there were some very useful
features that still aren't available (or available in a half-assed form) with
COBOL (e.g., controlled storage, recursion, macro preprocessor, put
list/edit/data stream output, in-line subroutines/functions).
```

#### ↳ Re: The Demise of COBOL Part II

- **From:** tim.oxler@NOSPAMteo-computer.com (Tim Oxler)
- **Date:** 1998-07-14T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol

```
john@ccpl.carr.lib.md.us wrote:

>Now, what is wrong with the alphabet soup of standard bodies (j4, g4, 9x
>etc.) appropriating the zippiest features of all existing languages and
…[11 more quoted lines elided]…
>

Having already read Bill's reply, I have to agree and say the same
thing.  I was also trained in PL/I, but found few shops that used PL/I
when I got out of school.  PL/I didn't prove to businesses to have
enough added value to warrant a switch to PL/I.  And yes, alot of that
had to do with COBOL already being dominate on big iron.

C/C++/VB didn't even try an attempt to unseat COBOL on mainframe.  But
they proliferated in and with the emergence of other platforms.  If
PL/I would have taken a similiar strategy, it could have been a major
or dominate player on these other platforms, and then leveraged that
onto mainframe.  But it didn't.

>The new COBOL will face the same problem. The enthusiasts who want to cram in
>every available feature from all these other languages will in fact use the
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>

I don't agree that it's the same problem, but yes, it is easier to
write C++ in C++.  (I assume you mean to not mix languages in an
application system).

>
>What exactly IS the COBOL market? It is defined by three factors, legacy
…[14 more quoted lines elided]…
>

First, some new features have assisted in making legacy code better.
Especially EVALUATE.  I've taken a 1000 line CICS program with ripple
cascading IF STMTs into EVALUATEs dropping some 300 lines in the
process and made the code much easier to maintain and read.

As for the new standard, I think the idea of using libraries is a good
idea.  This should reduce a lot of redundancy and 97 home grown
routines that could have been and should have been done only one way.

As for OO, I suspect that it will be to COBOL what OLE is to MS WORD.
Most won't use it, most won't know how to use it, and most will be
very happy with it's mainstream use.

IBM mainframe programmers will have the luxury of only dealing with
the new standard.  COBOL II (85) is only Y2k compliant if you install
a patch for CURRENT-DATE.  It will loose total support by IBM on
2001/03.  All prior versions are not Y2k compliant.

I would say the opposite.  It's an opportunity to teach those old dogs
new tricks.  And NOT necessarily for OO programming, but new standard
programming.  While many seasoned 10-15yr programmers can perform work
at a faster rate than many programmers with 2yrs experience, many
still write top-down multiple GOTO, PERFORM-lesscode that looks
identical to common code written circa 1980.  This defeats the purpose
of the new standards.


Tim Oxler
TEO Computer Technologies Inc.
http://www.teo-computer.com
Take the Y2k Quiz
http://www.teo-computer.com/dev/quiz.html
```

## Thread: EVALUATE Statement doesn't work - Why? — 15 msgs

_Topics: [`Language features and syntax`](topics.md#syntax)_

### EVALUATE Statement doesn't work - Why?

- **From:** Claus Heiko Niesen <cniesen@iastate.edu>
- **Date:** 1998-07-10T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<35A635E8.1D4D@iastate.edu>`

```
Hello,

I tried using the following evaluate statement:

01 WSWA-PRIORITY  PIC X(6).

EVALUATE WSWA-PRIORITY
  WHEN 'HIGH'
    ...
  WHEN 'MEDIUM'
    ...
  WHEN 'LOW'
    ...
END-EVALUATE

When I compiled it I got the following error on each "WHEN" statement:
  "An invalid abbreviated relation condition was found."

All the documentation I looked through were indicating that this should
work fine.  The following evaluate does work fine:
 
EVALUATE TRUE
  WHEN WSWA-PRIORITY = 'HIGH'
   ...
  WHEN WSWA-PRIORITY = 'MEDIUM'
   ...
  WHEN WSWA-PRIORITY = 'LOW'
   ...
END-EVALUATE

Does anybody have an explanation why the first evaluate statement
doesn't work.  In case you want the following info I'm working with the
"IBM VS COBOL II Release 3.1" compiler.

Thanks a lot,
  Claus
```

>

You need to define the 88 levels as HIGH,MEDIUM and Low, and include
what the values are.  This statement will then work.

01WSWA-PRIORITY  PIC X(6).
    88  HIGH VALUE 'HIGH'.
    88  MEDIUM VALUE 'MEDIUM'.
    88  LOW VALUE 'LOW'.


>EVALUATE WSWA-PRIORITY
>  WHEN 'HIGH'

Ken,

I don't think "This statement will then work" if you're talking about
Claus' original statement.  He has quotes around the values in the WHEN
statements.   You don't use quotes when you're using condition names, only
when you're defining them.

##### ↳ ↳ Re: EVALUATE Statement doesn't work - Why?

- **From:** Claus Heiko Niesen <cniesen@iastate.edu>
- **Date:** 1998-07-10T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<35A670B3.7C35@iastate.edu>`
- **References:** `<35A635E8.1D4D@iastate.edu> <35A65BB3.5AF@ibm.net>`

```
Bal Oberoi wrote:
> ...
> If you do find the cause of the problem perhaps you would consider
> posting it here?
> ...

I figured out the cause of the problem.  All the time I was using
evaluate statements of the following kind:
01  WSWA-VARIABLE              PIC XXX VALUE 'YES'. 
01  WSWA-INDICATOR             PIC X   VALUE SPACES.
    88  WSWA-INDICATOR-OK              VALUE 'Y'.
    88  WSWA-INDICATOR-NOT-OK          VALUE 'N'.

EVALUATE TRUE
  WHEN WSWA-INDICATOR-0K
   AND WSWA-VARIABLE = 'YES'
    ...
  WHEN WSWA-INDICATOR-NOT-OK
   OR  WSWA-VARIABE = 'NO'
    ...
END-EVALUATE

In this case AND and OR are fine.  However, in my other situation the OR
does not work. (I was so unfortunate and tried to simplify things by
leaving the or out.)

EVALUATE WSWA-PRIORITY
  WHEN 'HIGH'
   OR  'H'
     ...
  WHEN 'MEDIUM'
   OR  'M'
     ...
  WHEN 'LOW'
   OR  'L'
    ...
END-EVALUATE

It would be nice to do things like that.

Thanks for all your help,
  Claus

Why don't you try the following?

	EVALUATE	WSWA-PRIORITY
	WHEN		'HIGH'
	WHEN		'H'
	    high priority stuff
	WHEN		'MEDIUM'
	WHEN		'M'
	    medium priority stuff
	WHEN		'LOW'
	WHEN		'L'
	    low priority stuff
	END-EVALUATE

This is what I think you want to do and is legal. If you really want to
code the "OR" I believe you can code:

	EVALUATE	WSWA-PRIORITY
	WHEN		('HIGH' OR 'H')
	    high priority stuff
.
.

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: EVALUATE Statement doesn't work - Why?

- **From:** Artur Reimann <reimann@ibm.net>
- **Date:** 1998-07-11T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<35A767C8.C4@ibm.net>`
- **References:** `<35A635E8.1D4D@iastate.edu> <35A65BB3.5AF@ibm.net> <35A670B3.7C35@iastate.edu>`

```
Claus Heiko Niesen wrote:
> 
> Bal Oberoi wrote:
…[40 more quoted lines elided]…
>   Claus

Claus,
you're right, it would be nice to write these kind of things.
Unfortunately, in COBOL 85, it is not allowed, it's just not valid
syntax. Your expectation is that every combination of selection subject
and selection object is valid as long as it results in a valid
condition.
The draft new standard does allow this. It introduces another kind of
section object called "partial expression", which is used to supplement
the corresponding selection subject to form a conditional expression.
This is just one example of many in the draft standard where the
language does what you intuitively think it does.
Artur
```

Working storage section

01   ws-priority     pic x(6).
      88   high        value "HIGH  ".
      88   medium   value "MEDIUM".
      88   low          value "LOW   ".



evaluate true
      when  high   ....
      when  medium  ...
      when  low  ...
end-evaluate.

DON'T TAKE MY WORD FOR ANY OF THIS GO TO POWERSEARCH AND SEARCH BY AUTHOR,
ENTER docdwarf@clark.net SORT BY DATE AND JUST READ THE FIRST 50 OR SO POSTING
THAT THIS OUTSTAND NG CONTRIBUTOR HAS MADE.

I just wanted to get to know this wonderful individual a little better!  From
reading some of the posting that he placed and other people replied I can see
how he would constantly be looking for work!  How underpaid and under
appreciated his little mind must be!

I have recently been having a little exchange in this NG with
docdwarf@clark.net.  He seems to feel like he is the self appointed Nazi
moderator of this and other NGs.  His wonderful contributions and they are
numerous (11,000) on a power search in Deja News consist of telling 10,000
people to post a rate when they offer jobs.  And in some cases telling people
to post a rate when they werent offering a job. And telling new people to
COBOL to "do your own homework". Some other accomplishments include (but are
not limited to sending anonomous emails as other people to back up his crappy
attitude).

I would just like everyone to stand and thank him for bettering the NG with
his presence.

Mr Anderson, my apologies if my postings annoy you but I do not have a
'clique'... quite the reverse, I believe that Oscar Wilde was correct
when he expressed concern about people agreeing with him.

Would you be willing to perform an experiment?  As I've stated
previously I've noticed that since I began posting my boilerplate the
overall number of job-postings containing rates has risen... I'll make
you an offer.  Pick a reasonable period of time... six weeks, three
months, what have you... and I'll stop posting the 'please post rates'
boilerplate.  During that time it will be up to you to count the number
of postings by headhunters both with and without rates; it is my
contention that as the time-period goes on the number of rateless
postings will increase.  During this period, of course, you'll be asked
to report on, say, a weekly basis, these numbers... I've been burned in
the past with promises of future 'compensation' for my activities, of
course.

DD

What I have done in the past was to send a direct EMail to the "offending"
recruiter about their lack of posting a rate.  Some of them have responded
with an apology, along with the rate information, but most of them have
responded with the typical "BS" line:  The rate depends on experience. 
That might be true, but there is ALWAYS a rate range for the position,
just like there is a salary range for permanent jobs.  Still, these
"narrow minded" recruiters refuse to post the rate range.  Up here in
Seattle, there is a jobs newsgroup, and the same problem exists. 
Fortunately, I have enough contacts to know what the going rates are.

I still say the best thing would be for ALL of us to send each offending
recuiter an EMail DEMANDING that they post the rate range.  If they come
back with the "DOE" BS, just respond "forcefully" that there is ALWAYS a
rate range for any consulting position.  This newsgroup's moderator has
always been kind enough to post a message to the "offending" recruiter
about posting a rate.  (From what I understand, he also sends the
recruiter an EMail).  However, it appears that his efforts are "falling on
deaf ears", so to speak.  So, maybe each of us needs to send the recruiter
an EMail.
```

### Another Point of View - 'I Won't Post Rates'

Well, gang, yet another example of my 'bad taste' - there are those who
say posting private email is bad taste, don'cha know - but I look upon it
as a Public Service.  What's below is my latest reply; read it and...
choose for yourselves whether Mr Webb gets *your* bragsheet.

---begin quoted message

From docdwarf@clark.net Fri Jul 10 11:32:02 1998
Date: Fri, 10 Jul 1998 11:31:34 -0400 (EDT)
From: docdwarf@clark.net
To: gene_webb@bsg.stercomm.com
Subject: RE: Wanted: COBOL Programmer Dallas Tx (NetExpress and OO)

On Fri, 10 Jul 1998 gene_webb@bsg.stercomm.com wrote:

> 
> Well .... let me put it another way .... this is not a moderated group and if
> someone wants to post something in it and other people want to pursue it that is
> their choice.

This is quite true; if you wish to put up postings which, by their nature,
turn the most valuable applicants away from you then that is your choice.

If, on the other hand, you mention that this is an unmoderated group as a
way of saying 'you can't make me, nyah, nyah, nyah' then... well, perhaps
that is best not addressed.

> It is all about choice if someone doesn't wish to respond to my
> posting because it doesn't include a rate then they don't have too.  I am not
> sure what role you play that you feel other people should "comply". Bottom line
> .. you are the only one that has gotten upset about this posting of mine.
> Thanks for your input but what is done is done.

You were not asked to do anything about what 'has been done'... you were
asked to modify your behavior in the future.  Please post a rate, or range
of rates.

DD

> 
> -----Original Message-----
…[62 more quoted lines elided]…
> 
--- end quote

DD

Mr. Webb,

It has come to my attention that you feel that DD is the only one upset
at your postings of opening without rates. WRONG. Anyone worth his salt
in this business gets honked off by this practice. Do not be so naive as
to think that us crusty old professionals don't know what you are up to.
You already know what the client is paying, and you won't post the rate
in hopes of talking some poor slob into taking the position for less
than what it's worth. We've all met your type before, and you can't fool
us. If you don't want to post the rates, don't waste your time and our
bandwidth by posting ads to which NO ONE will respond.

thank you for your lack of cooperation,

Michael J. Ben-Tovim
President, Binary Systems Inc.

Here goes ... the rate! 30K - 99K. I don't think that potential applicants are
now more or less likely to apply or not apply.

The problem is that some people (the vocal minority, it appears) make a living
contract to contract and evidently get jobs from this NG. The only people that
bother to chime in are people that care whether a rate is posted or not.  I
know up until yesterday, I couldnt care less and I am sure that most people
don't use this as their primary means of finding a job ... they wouldnt be
working a whole lot if they did.

I can understand not wading through a lot of posting that do not meet your
salary requirements.

The problem I have with this thread (and this is my last post on the subject)
is that you can't force people. Every time someone posts an ad without a rate
we get a post from DD or Mickey (from reviewing posts still not convinced
that they are not one in the same, read the 'style' of the replies yourself).
 Now you have to wade through two (2) posts that you didnt want to read
thanks to DD and Mickey.  So wow gee now we are twice as far behind and
getting there 1/2 as fast much better!

I can't see that these frequent "LISTEN YOU CORPORATE TRASH RECRUITER
SUB-HUMAN I AM GOOD AND YOU DAM WELL BETTER POST RATES" have bettered the NG
at all..... for those programmers who garner a living from pulling these
posts think about that every time you have to read two or more posts for one
job because someone didnt post a rate! And it doesnt appear that that goes up
or down with the frequesnt flame for not posting the rates.

Thats all folks!  Those people interested the job will apply those who aren't
will not.  So I won't expect resumes from any of you that think DD is just
doing a fine and dandy job and keep up the good work!

- **From:** "Rick Smith" <ricksmith@aiservices.com>
- **Date:** 1998-07-11T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.software.year-2000,comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<O7Kp1.104$CH.558957@news1.atlantic.net>`

```

gene_webb@stercomm.com wrote in message <6o6e1i$bf$1@nnrp1.dejanews.com>...
>Here goes ... the rate! 30K - 99K. I don't think that potential applicants
are
>now more or less likely to apply or not apply.
>
Your posting of a range of rates does clear up one problem that occurred
to me, after reading your initial refusal to post rates.

Consider that a prospective employee, upon seeing a range this wide,
could reasonably conclude that, as they grow in experience, they will also
gain financially. Failing to post a rate or range of rates could allow one
to conclude that your intent is to hire someone then limit their opportunity
to grow financially within your organization; perhaps to control costs, at
their expense. After all, you could already have some employees who are
underpaid and posting rates publicly could cause problems with those
current employees.

In other words, posting rates means good employer; not posting rates
means bad employer!

Thank you,
---------------------------
Rick Smith
e-mail: < ricksmith@aiservices.com >

## Thread: What does FIELD1(2:1) mean? — 13 msgs

### What does FIELD1(2:1) mean?

- **From:** "Tim Mueller" <TIMmuellert@one.net>
- **Date:** 1998-07-10T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol,alt.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<35a6de9a.0@news.one.net>`

```
Given

01   FIELD1   PIC X(05)  VALUE '12378'
01   FILED2   PIC X(03)  VALUE 'ABC'

And the instruction

MOVE FIELD2(2:1) TO FIELD1(3:2)

What does the (2:1) and (3:2) tacked onto the field names mean?  I can't
find any references or examples of this in any of my books.  Thanks.
```

#### ↳ Re: What does FIELD1(2:1) mean?

- **From:** "Doug McKibbin" <dmckib@NOSPAM.goodnet.com>
- **Date:** 1998-07-10T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol,alt.cobol

```
On Fri, 10 Jul 1998 23:28:22 -0400, Tim Mueller wrote:

>Given
>
…[9 more quoted lines elided]…
>
It how COBOL can substring.  The two numbers are the starting position and
length.  In your example, (2:1) means starting with the second character
for a length of 1.
Regards,
Doug McKibbin

#### ↳ Re: What does FIELD1(2:1) mean?

- **From:** scomstock@aol.com (S Comstock)
- **Date:** 1998-07-11T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1998071104430500.AAA20186@ladder01.news.aol.com>`

```
Tim Mueller writes ...

>Given
>
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
>find any references or examples of this in any of my books.  Thanks.


You must have mighty old reference books, since this is part of the ISO/ANSI
'85 standard.
 The notation you are referring to is called "reference modification" in the
COBOL world ("substringing" in most other programming languages). The first
number represents the starting location within the named field; the second
number represents the number of bytes to participate. The colon must always be
specified to distinguish reference modification from subscripts or indexes.

Cheers,


Steve Comstock

What it means (other than the fact that it is direct field reference is) take
the first byte starting at offset two of field2 and move it to byte three of
field1 for two bytes.  Since the from field is only one byte I would expect
field one to end up looking like 12B_78 (underscore is a spaced) as the (3:2)
would act much like moveing a one byte character varaible to a two byte
character variable, that is it would right space fill.

#### ↳ Re: What does FIELD1(2:1) mean?

- **From:** mark0young@aol.com (Mark0Young)
- **Date:** 1998-07-11T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1998071116162300.MAA04353@ladder01.news.aol.com>`
- **References:** `<35a6de9a.0@news.one.net>`

```
In article <35a6de9a.0@news.one.net>, "Tim Mueller" <TIMmuellert@one.net>
writes:

>01   FIELD1   PIC X(05)  VALUE '12378'
>01   FILED2   PIC X(03)  VALUE 'ABC'
...
>MOVE FIELD2(2:1) TO FIELD1(3:2)

This is called "Reference modification" and is part of the '85 standard.

Reference modification implies that no data conversion takes place, but
otherwise acts similar to an elementary alphanumeric move.

FIELD2(2:1) designates the part of FIELD2 that starts in the second byte
position for length of 1.

FIELD1(3:2) designates the third byte of FIELD1 for length of 2, i.e., the
third and fourth bytes.

The above statement moves 'B' and a space over the '37'. (The space comes from
the destination of the MOVE being longer than the source, so COBOL
automatically treats this as if the sending field was extended by spaces.) The
resulting FIELD1 value is '12B 8'.

One thing not mentioned above is that one can leave off the length and it would
imply the rest of the field, e.g., MOVE FIELD2(2:1) TO FIELD1(3:) would imply
the third and subsequent bytes of FIELD1 will be modifed, e.g., as if MOVE
FIELD2(2:1) TO FIELD1(3:3) were coded, or MOVE FIELD2(2:1) TO FIELD1(3:1) MOVE
SPACES TO FIELD1(4:2).

Mark A. Young
```

#### ↳ Re: What does FIELD1(2:1) mean?

- **From:** "WOB" <wobconsult@sprynet.com>
- **Date:** 1998-07-12T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<6obeq3$ksb$1@juliana.sprynet.com>`
- **References:** `<35a6de9a.0@news.one.net>`

```
Tim,

    This is what is referred to as "Reference Modification". It was
introduced on the IBM Mainframe with Version/Release 3.1 of COBOL2 (late
80's). What manual are you using for reference? Me thinks you need a
different one OR a new instructor.

    Within the parenthesis, the numeric-value to the left of the colon is
the STARTING Position in the field. The rightmost numeric value is the
LENGTH. These hardcoded values can also be substituted with Data-Names
(preferably halfwords or fullwords for efficiency). Reference Modification
can ONLY be used on fields that are defined as DISPLAY or GROUP LEVELS
(which are inherently DISPLAY).

    I will probably be flogged by DD for addressing this question in the
first place, so I'll ask you this only ONE time ===> PLEASE DO YOUR OWN
HOMEWORK.

Thank You,

WOB,
Atlanta

#### ↳ Re: What does FIELD1(2:1) mean?

- **From:** Grehom@my-dejanews.com
- **Date:** 1998-07-12T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol,alt.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<6oa632$nn3$1@nnrp1.dejanews.com>`
- **References:** `<35a6de9a.0@news.one.net>`

```
In my AcuCobol-85 manual it's referred to as 'reference modification' .
I quote from my manual (sorry Acu :)  Reference Modification is a method of
dynamically redefining a data item at execution to refer to just part of it

General format

data-name ( leftmost-position : [length] )

Syntax rules:

1) both 'leftmost-position' and 'length' are arithmetic expressions. 2)
unless otherwise specified reference modification is allowed anywhere a data
item of the class alphanumeric is permitted. 3) 'Data-name' may be qualified
or subscripted.  Reference modification is done after both qualification and
subscripting.

This feature is a real boon - means some of the most murky pieces of cobol
can be written in a clear concise fashion - no more redefines, redefines,
redefines

for your example data  FIELD1  FIELD2  BEFORE 12378  ABC  AFTER 12B 8  ABC
note the space 'cos target field longer than source and Cobol space fills
then.

In article <35a6de9a.0@news.one.net>,
  "Tim Mueller" <TIMmuellert@one.net> wrote:
> Given

…[13 more quoted lines elided]…

##### ↳ ↳ Re: What does FIELD1(2:1) mean?

- **From:** mark0young@aol.com (Mark0Young)
- **Date:** 1998-07-13T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1998071301013800.VAA18777@ladder03.news.aol.com>`
- **References:** `<35aedf16.2236381@nntp.ix.netcom.com>`

```
In article <35aedf16.2236381@nntp.ix.netcom.com>, gvwmoore@ix.netcom.com (G
Moore) writes:

>hmm. i think you use a FIELD2:2:1, but in any case, i
>dont know if you can move 1 character into a 2 character
>position.

No, the syntax is fieldname(start:length) or fieldname(start:).

Like group moves, moves using reference modification are treated like
alphanumeric elementary moves but without data conversion. That means that if
the destination is longer than the source, the bytes in the destination after
the bytes received from the source will be filled with spaces.

Mark A. Young
```

## Thread: VA COBOL OS/2 V2.2 Debugging — 2 msgs

### VA COBOL OS/2 V2.2 Debugging

- **From:** "Steve Richards" <steve@aducredit(nospam).com>
- **Date:** 1998-07-10T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol

get an "over punch" (bad decimal data) error. Right now the thing pops
up the exception window and when I select "EXAMINE/RETRY" the whole
debugger session ends. My thought is that I should be placed back at the

#### ↳ Re: VA COBOL OS/2 V2.2 Debugging

- **From:** vbandke@bsp-gmbh.com (Volker Bandke)
- **Date:** 1998-07-12T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<F8fMbxuvNgmM-pn2-j7i58zPKIiG1@bspw0103.bsp.de>`
- **References:** `<fgrirnqhperqvgpbz.evw0840.pminews@222.238.238.3>`

```
On Fri, 10 Jul 1998 17:24:04, "Steve Richards" <steve@aducredit(nospam).com> wrote:

> Could someone explain how the VA COBOL debugger IDBUG should work when I
> get an "over punch" (bad decimal data) error. Right now the thing pops
> up the exception window and when I select "EXAMINE/RETRY" the whole
> debugger session ends.

From the README file of the PL/I Compiler (which uses the same debugger:)

---------------------------------  begin copy ----------------------------------
   C.1. Debugger
        --------

        a) Specify the /TEST and /GONUMBER options when you compile your
           application for debugging.

        b) Monitoring of expressions when the debugger is stopped
           at the main entry to the program is NOT supported.
           Unpredictable results may occur, and you may not be able
           to monitor expressions during the rest of the debugging
           session.

        c) Monitor information should NOT be saved in the debugger
           program profiles. If monitor information is saved in the
           program profiles and the program profiles are used
           during RESTART or a subsequent debugging session,
           unpredictable results may occur.

           To prevent monitor information from being saved, select:

           options->debugger settings->program profiles->select information

           and ensure that 'MONITOR' is not selected.

        d) Occasionally, you may see strange behavior in the debugger,
           such as failing to start, shutting down when stepping, etc.
           This can occur when the debugger Program Profile files
           -- which save information about previous debug sessions, such as
           window positions, breakpoints set... -- become corrupted. If the
           debugger exhibits such behavior, these Program Profile files
           should be erased.  These files have an @ sign in the
           extension (e.g., PDEBUG.@ox, or MYPROG.@op).
           On OS/2, their default location is in the OS2 subdirectory on the
           drive where OS/2 was installed (e.g., C:\OS2).

        e) If MMPM/2 is installed, the debugger may shut down when it
           tries to make a beep sound.  (The Warp operating system
           installs MMPM/2 by default.)  To avoid this problem, run the
           debugger in Synchronous PM Debugging mode or use DINSTSND.CMD
           to disable the sound portion of MMPM/2.  (You can enable
           sound again by running INSTSND.CMD.)  There is an APAR for
           Warp (PJ22061).

        f) If the Desktop Automatic Lockup feature is enabled and the
           debugger is active, the system may lock up when the timer
           expires.  Currently, the only solution is to reboot. To
           avoid this, disable the lockup feature (e.g., via the
           desktop settings notebook) before using the debugger.

        g) The debugger ignores the date attribute when evaluating expressions.

---------------------------------------- end copy --------------------------------------------------------

HTH
```

## Thread: A Scientific Experiment... Almost! — 10 msgs

### A Scientific Experiment... Almost!

- **From:** The Goobers <docdwarf@erols.com>
- **Date:** 1998-07-11T00:00:00

```
Alright, gang... the following is a reply I sent to Mr Anderson
regarding a proposal I put to the group:

--begin quote
David Anderson wrote:
> 
> Dear DD
> 
> I think you have hit upon and excellent idea.

I *did*?  Well, a blind chicken sometimes find grain, I guess.

> I agree to your proposal.
> It is only fair that to be critical I should be willing to do a small
> amount of work.  How about the 3 month period between July 15th and
> October 15th.

*Most* fair of you... you're on!

> 
> I agree that on each weekend I will count all postings by headhunters
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> of posting this to the newsgroup.

Fairness *and* regularity... have you thought about getting a job as a
laxative?

> 
> Thank you for your sporting attitude. A scientific approach to all of
> this suits me much better!

Hey, I'm a coder and I *know* how often I've been proven wrong... the
only reason I can tell where mistakes are being made is because I've
usually made them.  We've had an evaluation of a situation, a
proposal... now time for observation and analysis.

... can being so reasonable get us banned from the UseNet?

DD
--end quote

Well, here we have it... comes 15 July 1998 you'll no longer see me
boilerplating the headhunters... and time will tell whether I need to do
this on a regular basis.

Of course, the experiment discounts the pimps who've already fallen into
the habit of posting with rates due to my lambasting... but I am sure
that newbies will show up.  In the interest of fairness, of course, I
would request that other folks do not post my boilerplate.

Le the Survey Begin!

DD
```

>> > that a "Stay" or even a "Pardon" has been issued, they don't want to

Off topic? Not at all!

You were discussing analogies to COBOL programming. As I see it, you
discussed the importance of abiding by standards, even when they may
not seem to apply. For instance, the so-called, one-time program, although
it may be killed after use, it may also be spared for another day.

What about those germs? The short variable names that so frequently
creep into programs. You know the ones I'm talking about: X1, X2, etc.
As long as they remain on the skin; that is, used for design decisions
and modeling, there is no problem; but we must not allow them to infect
the final program.

Keep up this relevant discussion and we will all learn more.
---------------------
Rick Smith
e-mail: < ricksmith@aiservices.com >
```

## Thread: Ignoring Duplicates — 21 msgs

### Ignoring Duplicates

- **From:** cslvt@hotmail.com
- **Date:** 1998-07-11T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<6o85rb$c44$1@nnrp1.dejanews.com>`

```
Hi folks,
I'm writing a program (COBOL 74) that, among other things, reads in records
from a file, applies some conditions to it and then stores the data in an
array.  One condition is that duplicate records should be ignored.  Only the
newest (closest to the end of the file) should be stored.  My first instinct
was to compare each record to all the other records, but I'm having problems
with intrementing the input (I'm a master programmer by no means). Any
suggestions or direction?

Kam

-----== Posted via Deja News, The Leader in Internet Discussion ==-----
http://www.dejanews.com/rg_mkgrp.xp   Create Your Own Free Member Forum
```

#### ↳ Re: Ignoring Duplicates

- **From:** dilbert_programmer@my-dejanews.com
- **Date:** 1998-07-11T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<6o886k$f51$1@nnrp1.dejanews.com>`
- **References:** `<6o85rb$c44$1@nnrp1.dejanews.com>`

```
In article <6o85rb$c44$1@nnrp1.dejanews.com>,
  cslvt@hotmail.com wrote:
> Hi folks,
> I'm writing a program (COBOL 74) that, among other things, reads in records
…[11 more quoted lines elided]…
>
If it is possible can you sort the input file by the key you are trying to
compare.  It then becomes relatively simple to


- create a save record area
- initialize it to low-value or something
loop
   - read a record
   - save the key/record
   - is the record key the same as the last key
      - no
        - is the save area low-values
          - no - add the saved record to your array
          - yes - move current record to save area

      - yes replace save record with new record
end loop

If you are putting this into an array I hope the file isnt too big.

Another option assuming the file isng to big is

read a record
search the array for the same key if it found replace that element
if it is not found just add it to the array

-----== Posted via Deja News, The Leader in Internet Discussion ==-----
http://www.dejanews.com/rg_mkgrp.xp   Create Your Own Free Member Forum
```

When sorting using DFSORT use the EQUALS option to ensure that the
specific order of records is maintained.

#### ↳ Re: Ignoring Duplicates

- **From:** Grehom@my-dejanews.com
- **Date:** 1998-07-12T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<6oa89h$sho$1@nnrp1.dejanews.com>`
- **References:** `<6o85rb$c44$1@nnrp1.dejanews.com>`

```
I'm a Cobol professional of fifteen years standing and when I read this I
thought sounds easy enough - but then I thought 'search' array for existing
key value and merely overwrite duplicates with newer later value, appending
new keys to end of array.  If you wanted to get clever could use 'search all'
but this requires that key is in sorted order so means a fair amount of
playing around inserting new values into existing array to keep it in sorted
order. I'm now going to commit sacrilege on a Cobol news group entry and say
if your new to Cobol try and learn Perl as well/instead. (see
http://language.perl.com/index.html) a short program like:

    #!/usr/bin/perl -w
    $key_start = 3;    # constant stating where on record key starts
    $key_length = 10;; # constant stating how long key is
    while (<>) {
        $key = substr($_,$key_start,$key_length);
        $array{$key} = $_;
    }
    foreach (@array) {
        print;
    }

would do it all!!  available on most machines and operating systems.

In article <6o85rb$c44$1@nnrp1.dejanews.com>,
  cslvt@hotmail.com wrote:
> Hi folks,
> I'm writing a program (COBOL 74) that, among other things, reads in records
…[11 more quoted lines elided]…
>

Easy: write the data to an ISAM file keyed on what would be
considered duplicates - rewriting later records when they

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Ignoring Duplicates

- **From:** Bill Lynch <wblynch@att.net>
- **Date:** 1998-07-12T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<6obvvj$238@bgtnsc03.worldnet.att.net>`

```
Dave Johnson wrote:
> 
> Richard Plinston wrote in message <3298192.75223.8946@kcbbs.gen.nz>...
…[26 more quoted lines elided]…
> a write just loaded the index block.

ISAM? Are you running on a PC platform? Sounds like a good idea, writing
to a keyed file and reading it in when done. Since the spec calls for
retaining the newest, i.e., the one closest to EOF, I'd precede every
WRITE with a DELETE for the key to eliminate the test for duplicate key,
read for update & rewrite. YMMV

Bill Lynch

> 
> DaveJ.

>> >> > array.  One condition is that duplicate records should be ignored.

>> >> > with intrementing the input (I'm a master programmer by no means).
Any
>> >> > suggestions or direction?
>> >
>> >Easy: write the data to an ISAM file keyed on what would be
>> >considered duplicates - rewriting later records when they
>> >occur, then read the final file into the array.


As an implementation of the "Easy" technique (maybe not so "easy" for a
non-master programmer?), here is an example of the coding methodology I have
used successfully in the past to save the most recent duplicate key records
from a sequential file into an ISAM file for subsequent loading of a table
(note that this works most efficiently if there are not an overly large
number of duplicates):

MAIN-CONTROL.
    OPEN INPUT SEQ-FILE.
    OPEN OUTPUT ISAM-FILE.
    CLOSE ISAM-FILE.
*       above 2 lines assures an empty isam file to start with
    OPEN I-O ISAM-FILE.
    MOVE "NO" TO SEQ-FILE-EOF-SW.
     READ SEQ-FILE INTO ISAM-FILE-REC
        AT END MOVE "YES" TO SEQ-FILE-EOF-SW.
   PERFORM DUPE_LOOP UNTIL SEQ-FILE-EOF.
    CLOSE SEQ-FILE ISAM-FILE.
    OPEN INPUT ISAM-FILE.
    MOVE "NO" TO ISAM-FILE-EOF-SW.
    READ ISAM-FILE NEXT RECORD
        AT END MOVE "YES" TO ISAM-FILE-EOF-SW.
    PERFORM TABLE-FILL-AND-PROCESS
        UNTIL ISAM-FILE-EOF.
    CLOSE ISAM-FILE.
    .....  perform main-line logic here that uses your table
    STOP RUN.

DUPE_LOOP.
    WRITE ISAM-FILE-REC
        INVALID KEY
            MOVE SEQ-FILE-REC TO ISAM-FILE-REC
            READ ISAM-FILE
                INVALID KEY
                    DISPLAY "......... READ ABEND INFO"
                    STOP RUN
            END-READ
            MOVE SEQ-FILE-REC TO ISAM-FILE-REC
            REWRITE ISAM-FILE-REC
                INVALID KEY
                    DISPLAY "......... REWRITE ABEND INFO"
                    STOP RUN.
    READ SEQ-FILE INTO ISAM-FILE-REC
        AT END MOVE "YES" TO SEQ-FILE-EOF-SW.

TABLE-FILL-AND-PROCESS.
    ....  do whatever you are going to do with this unique entry into your
table
    READ ISAM-FILE NEXT RECORD
        AT END MOVE "YES" TO ISAM-FILE-EOF-SW.


>> >
>> Yes, removes all the 'how many do I expect' problems you'd get with
tables.
>> Anyone got any thoughts on the method, eg whether you try an insert and
trap
>> the 'duplicate key', or read first. According to the last sysprog I
worked
>> with,
>> you were better off reading first as this loaded data and index blocks,
>> whereas
>> a write just loaded the index block.


Reading first would probably be most efficient if there is a relatively
large number of duplicate key records involved.  In that case, I would
replace the DUPE-LOOP paragraph in the sample I have given above with
something like the following:

DUPE-LOOP.
   READ ISAM-FILE
       INVALID KEY
            MOVE SEQ-FILE-REC TO ISAM-FILE-REC
            WRITE ISAM-FILE
                INVALID KEY
                    DISPLAY "......... WRITE ABEND INFO"
                    STOP RUN
            END-WRITE
       VALID KEY
            MOVE SEQ-FILE-REC TO ISAM-FILE-REC
            REWRITE ISAM-FILE
                INVALID KEY
                    DISPLAY "......... REWRITE ABEND INFO"
                    STOP RUN
            END-REWRITE.
    READ SEQ-FILE INTO ISAM-FILE-REC
        AT END MOVE "YES" TO SEQ-FILE-EOF-SW.

>
>ISAM? Are you running on a PC platform? Sounds like a good idea, writing
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>read for update & rewrite. YMMV


In the case of always DELETE and then WRITE, I would replace the DUPE-LOOP
paragraph in the sample I have given  with something like this (but I have
no feel for the relative efficiency of this method):

DUPE-LOOP.
   DELETE ISAM-FILE RECORD
       INVALID KEY
*    does not matter if record to be deleted does not exist!
            NEXT SENTENCE.
    MOVE SEQ-FILE-REC TO ISAM-FILE-REC.
    WRITE ISAM-FILE
            INVALID KEY
                DISPLAY "......... WRITE ABEND INFO"
                STOP RUN.
    READ SEQ-FILE INTO ISAM-FILE-REC
        AT END MOVE "YES" TO SEQ-FILE-EOF-SW.

>
>Bill Lynch
>
>>
>> DaveJ.
```

```
In message <<usQaXXjr9GA.255@upnetnews05>> "Dennis J. Minette" <d.minette@computer.org> writes:
> >
> >ISAM? Are you running on a PC platform? Sounds like a good idea, writing

Umm, yes, PC, for the last nearly 20 years if CP/M, MP/M and
other 8 bit and 16 bit platforms count as Personal Computers.

> >to a keyed file and reading it in when done. Since the spec calls for
> >retaining the newest, i.e., the one closest to EOF, I'd precede every
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
> no feel for the relative efficiency of this method):

I would expect that DELETE and WRITE would be the least efficient
as the DELETE would update (or downdate) the index file only to
have it restored by the WRITE.  

It would be possible to always do a REWRITE and do a WRITE if
this fails, possibly the most efficient, but would look a
little odd, especially to those who think that a READ is
required first.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Ignoring Duplicates

_(thread depth: 6)_

- **From:** Binyamin_Dissen@theoffice.net (Binyamin Dissen)
- **Date:** 1998-07-13T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<35b6181a.34909854@news.netvision.net.il>`
- **References:** `<6oa89h$sho$1@nnrp1.dejanews.com> <3298192.75223.8946@kcbbs.gen.nz> <6obedt$7ou$3@heliodor.xara.net> <6obvvj$238@bgtnsc03.worldnet.att.net> <usQaXXjr9GA.255@upnetnews05>`

```
The easiest and fastest way to do this is sort of:

    SD  SORT-FILE .....
    01  SORT-REC.
        05   KEY-FIELD   ....
        05   remaining fields ....
        05   INPUT-SEQUENCE  PIC S9(8) COMP.


    77  INPUT-COUNTER   PIC  S9(8) COMP SYNC VALUE 0.
    01  SAVE-RECORD .....               

        SORT  SORT-FILE
            ASCENDING KEY KEY-FIELD INPUT-COUNTER  
            INPUT PROCEDURE  IN-PROC
            OUTPUT PROCEDURE OUT-PROC.

   IN-PROC SECTION.
        Open files, etc.
        READ  source-file AT END SET eof-detected TO TRUE.
        PERFORM  UNTIL  eof-detected
              ADD 1 TO INPUT-COUNTER
              MOVE input-fields TO sort-fields
              MOVE INPUT-COUNTER TO INPUT-SEQUENCE
              RELEASE SORT-REC
              READ source-file AT END SET eof-detected TO TRUE.
        Close files.

    OUT-PROC SECTION.
        Open files, etc.
        RETURN SORT-REC INTO SAVE-RECORD AT END SET eof-detected TO TRUE.
        PERFORM  UNTIL  eof-detected
              IF  KEY-FIELD OF SAVE-RECORD NOT EQUAL KEY-FIELD OF SORT-REC
                  MOVE SAVE-RECORD TO output-fields
                  WRITE output-file
              END IF
              MOVE SORT-REC TO SAVE-REC
              RETURN SORT-REC AT END SET eof-detected TO TRUE.
        MOVE SAVE-RECORD TO output-fields
        WRITE output-file
        Close files.

Probably a few syntax errors here and there, but using ISAM to sort a file is
probably about the slowest way to do it. And if there is support for SORT
DUPLICATES then USING / OUTPUT PROCEDURE will do the job.
```

In my experience, especially with PCs!

I had numerous problems with memory fragmentation when
using the SORT verb. This created a problem wherein
the program would run to completion but the records
were not correctly sorted. By replacing the SORT with
an ISAM file, the problem was solved.

```
 One condition is that duplicate records should be ignored.  Only the
>newest (closest to the end of the file) should be stored.  My first instinct
>was to compare each record to all the other records, but I'm having problems
>with intrementing the input (I'm a master programmer by no means). Any
>suggestions or direction?



umm, yes. do the following (at your own risk) (pseudo code):

errm. bug report: write buffer should mean add that buffer
to your array.

declare alternating-buffer-variable
declare has-first-record-been-read
declare 2 record buffers

set alternating-buffer-variable to 1
set has-first-record-been-read to false

perform until end-of-file
	evaluate alternating-buffer and has-first-record
	when 1 and true
		read into buffer1 a record
		compare buffer2 to buffer1
		if different buffers, write buffer2
		set alt-buffer to 2
	when 1 and false
		read into buffer1 a record
		set alt-buffer to 2
	when 2 and true
		read into buffer2 a record
		compare
		if dif, write buf1
		set alt to 1
	end-evaluate
	set has-first to true
perform final-record.

end program


final-record.
evaluate alternating-buffer and has-first-record
	when 1 and true
		read into buffer1 a record
		compare buffer2 to buffer1
		if different fields, write buffer2
		set alt-buffer to 2
	when 1 and false
		read into buffer1 a record
		set alt-buffer to 2
	when 2 and true
		read into buffer2 a record
		compare
		if dif, write buf1
		set alt to 1
	end-evaluate

hmm. good point. before that code is executed, you
should write the entire record structure in ascending
order to a temporary file. and you might as well
apply the conditions (excluding the duplicate condition)
to that file, so that you dont have to read too many records
the second time around.

#### ↳ Re: Ignoring Duplicates

- **From:** bgwillia@vcu.edu (Boyce G. Williams, Jr.)
- **Date:** 1998-07-13T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<35aa03eb.2776838@usenet.acw.vcu.edu>`
- **References:** `<6o85rb$c44$1@nnrp1.dejanews.com>`

```
cslvt@hotmail.com wrote:

>Hi folks,
>I'm writing a program (COBOL 74) that, among other things, reads in records
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
>suggestions or direction?

Let's see:  you want to process a file that will ignore duplicate
records except for the last record of the group.  Simple.

The trick to this is how to ID the last record of a group of records.
If you have a date or counter already in the record that makes each
record unique and in sequence desired then you can sort by your
"duplicate" primary key then by date/counter.  If you don't or the
file was just a "collection" file (the most recent data was the last
physical record entered) then assign a number to an unused field or
move the record to a working-stroage group with some extra fields at
the end to pad with and increment a number to the pad.  As long you
are not saving the record you don't have a problem.

Normally the code looks like this:

000-Mainline.
1.  Open the files.
2.  Initialize the variable fields.
3.  SORT file ascending key primary
              ascending key counter (or date, if used)
        input procedure 200-process-file-inputfile
       output procedure 300-process-file-sortfile.
4.  Close the files.

200-process-file-inputfile.
1.  Do a priming read.
Perform until end-of-file:
    2.  Assign an incremented counter to the record
          (assuming there is nothing that makes each record unique
           and in the order read already) 
    3.  Release the record
    4.  read the next record.
end-perform.

300-process-file-sortfile
1.  Do a priming return.
Perform until end-of-file:
	2. Assign the 1st group's primary key to a Working-stroage field.
	Perform until end-of-file
        or 1st group's primary key differs 
        from its Working-stroage counterpart:
		3.  Assign the record to a second group with the
               identical layout.
		4.  Return the next record.
	end-perform
	5.  Process the second group.
end-perform

This assumes you're using the "READ...INTO"/"RETURN...INTO" method,
hence the need for two identical layouts in WORKING-STORAGE.  The rest
is left as an exercise.

Boyce G. Williams, Jr.

 .--------------------------------------------------------------------.
 | "People should have two virtues:  purpose- the courage to envisage |
 | and pursue valued goals uninhibited by the defeat of infantile     |
 | fantasies, by guilt and the failing fear punishment;  and wisdom- a|
 | detached concern with life itself, in the face of death itself."   |
 |                                                     Norman F. Dixon|
 '--------------------------------------------------------------------'
```

- **From:** Len Lewandowski <leonardl@execpc.com>
- **Date:** 1998-07-14T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<6ogsam$8a0@newsops.execpc.com>`
- **References:** `<6o85rb$c44$1@nnrp1.dejanews.com>`

```
Assuming you are on an IBM mainframe, sort will eliminate duplicate records by
itself.  I believe you use a sort sum???  Otherwise sort on the your key. Then
run the sorted file into your program and do normal break logic (saving the
input record & processing it on a key break) and remember to process you last
record since you will not have a normal key break.  Easy as pie.  Good luck.

#### ↳ Re: Ignoring Duplicates

- **From:** aacinstrjc@aol.com (AACInstrJC)
- **Date:** 1998-07-14T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1998071406271400.CAA19950@ladder01.news.aol.com>`
- **References:** `<6o85rb$c44$1@nnrp1.dejanews.com>`

```
Kam writes :
<<<Hi folks,
I'm writing a program (COBOL 74) that, among other things, reads in records
from a file, applies some conditions to it and then stores the data in an
array.  One condition is that duplicate records should be ignored.  Only the
newest (closest to the end of the file) should be stored.  My first instinct
was to compare each record to all the other records, but I'm having problems
with intrementing the input (I'm a master programmer by no means). Any
suggestions or direction? >>>

When you say that duplicates should be ignored you give me the impression that
there is a key field or fields identifiy the input record and if there is and
its numeric you may have an easy answer to your problem.   As a quick and
oversiplified example lets say we have have a file containing sales tax rates
for 50 states* in historical order.   A two digit state code identifies the
state and there are duplicates with the most current towards the rear of the
file.  If you do nothing more than :
         move in-state-rate to tab-state-rate(in-state-code)

the records will be placed in the proper order in the array and with the most
current overlaying the older records.

I couldn't really say any more without knowing how you identify dupilcates
coming from the input file.

Regards,
Jim Castro
```

## Thread: Why do Headhunters get upset when you ask for rates — 8 msgs

_Topics: [`Jobs, careers, recruiting, salary`](topics.md#jobs)_

### Why do Headhunters get upset when you ask for rates

- **From:** "Robert D. Jones" <rd_jones@bellsouth.net>
- **Date:** 1998-07-11T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<35A78BDC.3CD49AF8@bellsouth.net>`

```
I get tired of the attitude that headhunters have when they are asked
for rates. This news group has shown how childish they are. If I want to
employ a plumber, I am forced to pay whatever he sets as fair or market
price, not me. What choice do I have? Pay the rate or call someone else.
Cheaper usually means lesser quality.
```

#### ↳ Re: Why do Headhunters get upset when you ask for rates

- **From:** The Goobers <docdwarf@erols.com>
- **Date:** 1998-07-11T00:00:00

- **References:** `<35A78BDC.3CD49AF8@bellsouth.net>`

```
Robert D. Jones wrote:
> 
> I get tired of the attitude that headhunters have when they are asked
> for rates. This news group has shown how childish they are.

Mr Jones, in defense of the pimps, not all... I usually send two
notices, one public, one private email, with the boilerplate; I have
received many apologies and have seen subsequent postings which then
reflect the charter of the newsgroup.  It is like anything else... some
decent folks, some wretched ones.

> If I want to
> employ a plumber, I am forced to pay whatever he sets as fair or market
> price, not me. What choice do I have? Pay the rate or call someone else.
> Cheaper usually means lesser quality.

I *have* noticed that in Business In General there seems to be a game...
The One Who First Mentions A Number Loses.  To me it shows a kind of
childish insecurity in one's ability to bargain; it results in the
following interchange:

Me: 'Hmmmm... so the location is Atlanta, the duration is 6 months, the
kind of work is CICS/DB2... what kind of rate are they offering for this
kind of work?'

Pimp: 'Well, what kind of rate are you looking for?'

Me: 'Excuse me, that does not answer my question... I asked you first.' 
(notice the barely-contained 'nyah nyah nyah' in my reply... in formal
discourse, business or academic, I find the tactic of answering a
question with a question detestable)

DD
```

     "Why shouldn't I?" 

"Why did you do it again?"
  
     "Do you have a problem with that?"

## Thread: Regarding Mr. Webb — 19 msgs

### Regarding Mr. Webb

- **From:** stevewie@apk.dot.net (SkippyPB)
- **Date:** 1998-07-11T00:00:00

```
To the group,

Well I did a little search of messages posted to this newsgroup over
the past couple of months looking for our esteemed Mr. Webb (much like
he did in Deja News looking for DD) and found some interesting things.

First off, it seems he has been not only a contributor to this NG
answering questions concerning Net Express, but a questioner as well
receiving answers from others in this NG.

Secondly, I found the following (quoted exactly) by Mr. Webb in a
response to a job posting from a recruiter in the Dallas area: 

"This sounds like Frito Lay .... they still are only paying about 50%
of what other people pay ... 40-55k will get you someone with 3 or 4
years experince if that in today's wages ... duh"

It seems he is willing to criticize others for paying low wages, but
at least a rate was quoted and could be judged thusly and yet he is
unwilling to post a reasonable rate or range of rates!  This coupled
with his recent rantings and ravings about and against Mickey and DD
have led me to conclude that Sterling Commerce, Banking Systems
Division would not be an enjoyable place to work at any salary given
Mr. Webb's attitudes.  I think the word should be spread.  Having been
a manager myself, I would never have conducted myself in such a manner
before an audience of potential employees if I hoped to convince
someone to come and work for me.

But don't take my word for it.  Do your own search and draw your own
conclusions.  And Mickey and DD....keep on posting the rates notices.
It's appreciated.

Regards,


          ////
         (o o)
-oOO--(_)--OOo-
Everyone has a photographic memory. Some don't have film.
 Steve
```

why void main() should not be used.

constant reference to precedence tables to avoid subtle
problems - thrashed out over weeks in discussion groups.

capable tools.  They just do their job of getting systems running.
Bleeding edge programmers using less capable tools produce
less stable products and tend to need to discuss why it is
all going wrong.

Anyway, try discussing anything relevant (such as pros and
cons of GO TO) and you will get a number of postings bemoaning
the discussion because it makes them have to think or
something.    ;-)

:> we can't just slip in a new module whenever we feel like it.
Understood, but your original post said you had a
problem upgrading because management didn't like
the idea of having to shut down the application. 

However, seeings you can shut down the application
during a scheduled weekend maintenance then that
is the time to do the upgrade. The application, if
running, will cause a "lock" to be held on any
DLLs it may be using --- whether they are yours or
the operating system's. That is what you noticed
and which prompted your original post.

I think that is your best option.

Apologies should my original response have seemed
a little terse -- I was feeling somewhat grumpy
that day.

Cheers,

[snip]


-- Siegen 
---------------------- 
Please remove the letter "x" from my email address, should you wish
to email me.
(rodsp@comxcen.com.au)
---------------------
```

### job postings, gene webb, DD, and all readers of this newsgoup

- **From:** Bob Berman <bberman@netbox.com>

```
I think that Mr. Webb and many of the persons responding to him are
missing the issue here.

Job listings *should* be posted to the xx.jobs newsgroups or
alt.computer.consultants.ads, and not to a technical newsgroup such as
comp.lang.cobol.  Let the issue of disclosing rates be an issue in
*those* newsgroups, and not in this one !  Let this newsgroup be a forum
for sharing ideas, experiences, and techniques about Cobol programming,
differences in Cobol implementations, tools for effective business data
processing solutions, etc.

I, for one, don't mind if students ask questions, as long as it shows
they have done *some* research on their own before posting.  I enjoy
reading threads about organizational problems in corporations, whether
they be written humorously or sarcastically.  This is human interaction,
the same as if we were speaking to each other face-to-face.

DD and others - maybe a more effective approach would be to harass the
job posters about posting to this newsgroup at all - rather than asking
them to post a second time with rates.  

Food for thought - Regards to all

Bob Berman
```

With all due respect, Mr Berman, I must disagree with your suggestion...
but you expected that already, didn't you?

I view (rightly or wrongly, of course) this group to be a sort of
'programmer's playground'... but even when programmers play there's an
air of Work to it.  (Perhaps that is why I enjoy my trade... when it
gets *really* good the differentiation between Work and Play
disintergrates)  We joke, we kid, we lambast the newbies and call each
other poopie-heads... all in good fun, of course.

A pimp is always welcome, in my book, to ask if someone is interested in
working... but in 'our' playground this should be according to 'our'
rules.  Yes, we enjoy coding... but one needs a job, at times, and
finding a job needs a pimp... at times.  Dealings with pimps can be...
distasteful, to say the least (Mr Webb's recent postings being an
example... he's not even a pimp so he does it *exquisitely* badly) and
so should be kept as businesslike as possible... location of slot,
duration of slot, type of work and rate.  Anything else ('We're the nth
largest stable in the Universe, growing *really* fast and are known for
our proactive people-oriented...
something-or-other-buzzword-of-the-week' is something I have yet to find
anyone who needs).

Did this make any sense?  If so answer 'maybe'.

DD
```

I just caught up on my newsgroups and this has gotten way out of hand.  Lets
see what I can do to make it right.

I apologize to the group for not posting a rate.  I did not read all the way
down to 18.2 on the FAQ.  In addition like many corporate work places
discussing money is considered a taboo and I carried that thinking into my
posting. Maybe I should have said Rate: All You Can Get Them To Pay You!!!

I should have ignored the posting of private email between DD and myself and
not responded.	I guess that is the programmers social skills coming out in
me.

It is unfortunate that some people have now chosen not to target me but an
exceptionally fine company that I work for making slanderous remarks about
them. Just so everyone is clear: My opinons expressed in this newsgroup are
mine and mine alone.  They do not in any way reflect those of my employer.  I
didnt think I should really have to say this but based on the postings I
think it only prudent.

I love my job, I love exchanging information with other professionals. I will
continue to post in a productive manner as I have done in the past.

As you will notice I am no longer using my work email account for posting
here.  Unfortunately I think this is only prudent after the personal attacks
on my employer by people that disagree with me.  I do not represent
everything about my company anymore than any of you do. Please send email to
my new email account and I will response as appropriate.

<a id="t-6a94c79ef0"></a>
## Thread: What does FIELD1(2:1) mean? — 2 msgs

### Re: What does FIELD1(2:1) mean?

- **From:** <@thevision.net>
- **Date:** 1998-07-11T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol,alt.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<6o6s42$e80$1@news.eli.net>`

```
It refers to part of the field; in this case the part that starts in position 2 and
is 1 byte long. After the move field1 will be "12B 78", (note space)

The position is normal, not offset; first position is 1, not 0,


"Tim Mueller" <TIMmuellert@one.net> writes: > Given
> 
> 01   FIELD1   PIC X(05)  VALUE '12378'
…[12 more quoted lines elided]…
>
```

#### ↳ Re: What does FIELD1(2:1) mean?

- **From:** Detlef Lexut <DLexut@gdtsoft.com>
- **Date:** 1998-07-13T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol,alt.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<35AA28F4.318@gdtsoft.com>`
- **References:** `<6o6s42$e80$1@news.eli.net>`

```
@thevision.net wrote:
> 
> It refers to part of the field; in this case the part that starts in position 2 and
…[19 more quoted lines elided]…
> >

The resulting field will contain '12B_8' after move with RefMod.
```

<a id="t-20b49bdea1"></a>
## Thread: In Line perform in Evaluate — 6 msgs

_Topics: [`Language features and syntax`](topics.md#syntax)_

### In Line perform in Evaluate

- **From:** lvenick@aol.com (LVenick)
- **Date:** 1998-07-11T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1998071120083600.QAA04493@ladder03.news.aol.com>`

```
Is it possible to use an Inline-Perform with an Evaluate?-
 I'm tring to evaluate 4 different trans-codes, with each one triggering
a different routine.  It works fine when I use out-of-line performs ie:
EVALUATE TRANS-CODE
    WHEN '0'
         PERFORM 0-RTN THRU 0-EXIT
     WHEN '1'
          PERFORM.........
END-VALUATE
But if i try it as:
EVALUATE TRANS-CODE
     WHEN '0'
           PERFORM
                  ADD..........
                  MOVE.......
                  MOVE....
            END-PERFORM
      WHEN '1'
              PERFORM
                   ............
                   ............ 
               END-PERFORM
   END-EVALUATE

I get serious  syntax errors ......  
Can anyone help.
thanx,
Larry V (an eager student)
```
